Meanings of Salat and Salam
Defines the terms salat and salam in context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three meanings of salat depending on the subject (Allah, angels, humans) and define salam as safety.

Core Idea
Salat means supplication, but from Allah it is mercy, from angels it is forgiveness, from humans it is prayer.

The terms 'salat' and 'salam' are central to the act of sending blessings upon the Prophet. However, their meanings shift depending on who is performing the action. This lesson unpacks these nuanced definitions as presented in the Hanafi commentary, setting the foundation for understanding the command and virtue of sending salawat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Locate the terms 'salat' and 'salam' in the passage. Note that 'salat' is defined in three distinct ways based on the subject (Allah, angels, or humans).
The term 'salat' is polysemous in Arabic.
2
Distinguish meanings by subject
When attributed to Allah, 'salat' means mercy; when attributed to angels, it means seeking forgiveness; when attributed to humans, it means supplication (dua). Memorize these three meanings.
This distinction is crucial for understanding Quranic verses and hadith.
3
Define salam
The passage defines 'salam' as 'all types of safety' (kull qism ki salāmatī). This is the greeting of peace upon the Prophet.
'Salam' is often paired with 'salat' in the formula.
4
Note the Prophet's title
The Prophet is referred to as 'khatam an-nabiyyin' (seal of the prophets), emphasizing his finality. This is part of the formula of blessings.
The title is a reminder of his unique status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه: درود اور سلام ہو ہمارے سردار محمد پر جو خاتم النبین ہیں ، اور آپ کے پاک آل پر اور تمام صحابہ پر۔ تشريح : الصلوۃ : صلوۃ کے معنی دعا، لیکن اگر اس کی نسبت اللہ کی طرف ہو تو اس کے معنی رحمت کرنا ، اور فرشتے کی طرف ہو تو صلوۃ کے معنی استغفار کرنا۔ اور انسان کی طرف ہو تو اس کے معنی دعا ہے۔ سلام : ہر قسم کی سلامتی (۱) صلوۃ اور سلام کا ثبوت اس آیت میں ہے۔ ان الله و ملائكته يصلون على النبي يايها اللذين آمنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسليما آیت ۵۶ سورۃ الاحزاب ۳۳ - ترجمہ: اللہ اور فرشتے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود بھیجتے ہیں اس لئے ایمان والو تم بھی ان پر درود اور سلام بھیجو۔ اس آیت میں صلوۃ وسلام دونوں پڑھنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ بلکہ فضیلت کی بات یہ ہے کہ خود اللہ تعالی اس کام کو کرتے ہیں۔ پھر تو فضیلت کا کیا کہنا! علماء فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت آدم کو فرشتوں سے سجدہ کروایا اس سے زیادہ فضیلت درود وسلام میں ہے ۔ کیونکہ درود اور سلام خود اللہ تعالی فرماتے ہیں۔ ع بعد از خدا توئی بزرگ قصہ مختصر
Translation: Blessings and peace be upon our leader Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and upon his pure family and all his companions. Elaboration: As-Salat: the meaning of salat is supplication, but if it is attributed to Allah, its meaning is to show mercy; if attributed to angels, its meaning is to seek forgiveness; and if attributed to humans, its meaning is supplication. As-Salam: all types of safety. (1) The evidence for salat and salam is in this verse: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet. O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace' (Surah al-Ahzab 33:56). Translation: Allah and the angels send salat upon the Prophet, so O believers, send salat and salam upon him. In this verse, the command to recite both salat and salam is given. Rather, the excellence is that Allah Himself does this act. Then what can be said of its virtue! Scholars say that this is greater than the virtue of commanding the angels to prostrate to Adam, because salat and salam are performed by Allah Himself. After that, a Persian couplet: 'After God, you are great; the story is short.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'as-salat was-salam' from the sermon (khutbah) of the book. The author first provides a translation of the standard formula of blessings upon the Prophet, then elaborates on the technical meanings of 'salat' and 'salam' based on the doer. For 'salat', the meaning shifts depending on the subject: from Allah it is mercy, from angels it is seeking forgiveness, and from humans it is supplication. 'Salam' is defined as all types of safety. The author then cites Quranic evidence from Surah al-Ahzab (33:56), which commands believers to send both salat and salam. He emphasizes the great virtue of this act, noting that it surpasses even the prostration of angels to Adam because salat and salam are done by Allah Himself. The Persian couplet at the end poetically extols the Prophet's rank. This lesson is doctrinal and devotional, not directly a legal ruling, but it establishes the basis for the command to send salawat in prayer and daily life.

Key Terms
الصلوۃ (as-salat): Linguistically supplication; in religious context, from Allah means mercy, from angels means seeking forgiveness, from humans means blessing the Prophet.
السلام (as-salam): Safety or peace; the greeting of peace upon the Prophet.
خاتم النبیین (khatam an-nabiyyin): Seal of the prophets; meaning the final prophet after whom no new prophet will come.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'salat' mean when attributed to angels according to the text?
A) Mercy
B) Supplication
C) Seeking forgiveness
D) Peace

Key Takeaway
The term 'salat' takes on different meanings (mercy, forgiveness, supplication) depending on whether it is from Allah, angels, or humans, while 'salam' consistently means safety.

The Quranic Command to Send Blessings
Cites Quranic evidence and extols the virtue of sending salawat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the Quranic evidence for sending salawat (al-Ahzab 33:56) and explain why this act is considered greater than the prostration of angels to Adam.

Core Idea
Sending blessings upon the Prophet is an act that Allah Himself performs, making it the greatest honor.

Having understood the meanings of salat and salam, this lesson examines the direct Quranic command to send them upon the Prophet. The verse not only obligates this act but also highlights its immense virtue, comparing it favorably to even the famous event of the angels prostrating to Adam.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Quranic verse
Find the verse from Surah al-Ahzab (33:56) quoted in the passage. Note that it contains two imperative verbs: 'صلوا' (send blessings) and 'سلموا' (greet with peace).
The verse is cited as the primary evidence.
2
Analyze the command
The verse commands believers to perform both salat and salam upon the Prophet. In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
The passage does not specify the exact fiqh category beyond 'hukm' (command).
3
Understand the virtue
The passage emphasizes that Allah Himself performs this act, and then scholars compare it to the prostration of angels to Adam, stating that sending salawat is even greater because it is done by Allah directly.
This underscores the immense honor.
4
Note the practical implication
This verse forms the basis for reciting salawat in various contexts, particularly in prayer (tashahhud) and upon hearing the Prophet's name.
The Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Four Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs
Lists and explains four nullifiers of masah over khuffs with textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four nullifiers of masah al-khuff, identify the evidence for each, and apply the ruling when a nullifier occurs.

Core Idea
Four events invalidate the mash over khuffs—know them to preserve your wudu.

In this lesson, we examine the four things that break the concession of wiping over khuffs. Understanding these nullifiers is essential for correctly performing wudu while wearing khuffs, as the mash becomes invalid and the feet must be washed. The text provides textual evidence from hadith and the practice of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is masah al-khuff (wiping over leather socks), a permissible alternative to washing feet during wudu for a limited time. The passage lists its nullifiers.
2
List the four nullifiers
The text states four: (1) anything that breaks wudu, (2) removal of the khuff (or most of the foot exiting), (3) water reaching most of one foot, (4) expiry of the time limit (one day for resident, three for traveler).
The third is stated 'ala al-sahih (on the correct view), indicating a difference of opinion.
3
Examine the evidence for each
For (1), hadith of Safwan: "except from janabah" implies other nullifiers. For (2), hadith of Mughirah: "as long as he does not remove them". For (3), the principle of not combining washing and wiping. For (4), hadith of Ali on jabirah (splint).
The proofs are ahad hadith, zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Determine the consequence of each nullifier
For (1), the entire wudu is broken. For (2)-(4), if wudu remains intact, only washing both feet is required; the rest of wudu is unaffected.
After the last three (2,3,4), only the feet need washing as per the text.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The third nullifier (water reaching most of one foot) is subject to difference among Hanafis. The author affirms it as the correct view. The mufta bihi is that it breaks the mash.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text

لغت : ساق الخف : موزہ کا جو حصہ پاؤں کی پنڈلی کے پاس رہتا ہے اس کو ساق الخف ، کہتے ہیں۔
ترجمه : (۲۳۲) [۳] ایک قدم کے اکثر حصہ کو پانی پہونچ جائے ہیچ مذہب یہی ہے۔ تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دھونا اور مسح جمع نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ اس لئے قدم کا اکثر حصہ بھیگ گیا تو ایک قدم کا غسل ہو گیا ، اس لئے دوسرے قدم کا مسح جمع کرنا درست نہیں ہے اس لئے دوسرے قدم کے موزے کو بھی نکال کر دھونا ہوگا۔ صیح مذہب یہی ہے ترجمه : (۲۳۳) [۴] مسح کی مدت ختم ہو جاوے، اگر ٹھنڈ سے پاؤں کے ضائع ہونے کا اندیشہ نہ ہو۔ تشریح : مسح کی مدت ایک دن یا تین دن ختم ہو جانے سے بھی مسح ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر پاؤں دھونے سے برف کی وجہ سے
پاؤں شل ہو جانے کا خطرہ ہو تو اب اس کا حکم جبیرہ [پٹی ] کا حکم ہو جائے گا کہ جب تک مجبوری رہے گی مسح کرتا رہے گا۔ وجه : عن على بن ابى طالب قال سألت رسول الله علي الله عن الجبائر يكون على الكسير ، كيف يتوضأ صاحبها و كيف يغتسل اذا اجنب ؟ قال يمسحان بالماء عليها في الجنابة و الوضوء ، قلت فان كان في برد يخاف على نفسه اذا اغتسل ؟ قال يمر على جسده ، و قرأ رسول الله الله و لا تقتلوا انفسكم ان الله كان بكم رحيما، ويتيمم اذا خاف (دار قطنی ، باب جواز امسح على الجبائر ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۸۶۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سردی کا خوف ہو تو جنابت کے لئے بھی جسم کو صرف پونچھ لے، اور اس سے بھی زیادہ خوف ہو تو تیم کر لے۔
ترجمه : (۲۳۴) اور ان تین اخیر کے بعد صرف پاؤں دھو لینا کافی ہے۔ تشریح : تین اخیر سے مراد ہے کہ [1] موزہ کھل جائے [۲] اکثر قدم پانی سے بھیگ جائے [۳] یا موزے کی مدت ختم ہو
جائے ، اور وضو موجود ہو تو پورا وضولوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ، صرف پاؤں دھولے اور موزہ پہن لے اتنا ہی کافی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن ابراهيم قال : اذا نزعتهما فاغسل قدميك ، و به یأخذ الثورى . (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نزع الخفین بعد امسح ، ج اول ص ۲۱۰ نمبر ۸۱۳ ) (۲) عن رجل من اصحاب النبي الله في الرجل يمسح على خفيه ثم يبدو له فينزعهما قال يغسل قدميه (سن للبیھقی ، باب من خلع خفیه بعد مامسح علیهما ص۲۳۴، نمبر۱۳۷۰) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ موزہ کھل جائے تو دونوں قدم کو دھوئے۔
Section: What Invalidates Wiping over the Khuff. Four things invalidate wiping over the khuff: (230) Everything that invalidates wudu; (231) Removal of the khuff, even if most of the foot exits to the leg of the khuff; (232) Water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff, according to the correct view; (233) Expiry of the time period, provided one does not fear the loss of his foot from cold; (234) After the last three, washing his two feet only suffices. (235) It is not permissible... The commentary explains each: (230) Anything that breaks wudu also breaks the mash, e.g., hadath or janabah. (231) If the entire khuff is removed or most of the foot comes out, mash is broken; one must wash the feet and re-wear the khuff; complete wudu need not be repeated. (232) If water reaches most of one foot, washing and mashing cannot be combined, so both khuffs must be removed and feet washed. (233) When the duration expires (one day for resident, three for traveler), mash is broken; if cold is feared, the ruling of a splint (jabirah) applies—mash continues until the excuse ends. (234) After these three events (removal, water, expiry), only washing the feet is sufficient; the rest of wudu remains intact.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling with proofs regarding the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs. The author first lists the four: (1) anything that invalidates wudu, (2) removal of the khuff (even if most of the foot exits to the shin part), (3) water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff (on the correct view), and (4) expiry of the time limit (provided no fear of harm from cold). The commentary then expands each. For the first, it states that events like hadath (passing wind, urine, etc.) and janabah break the mash just as they break wudu. Proof is given from the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal that the Prophet allowed wiping for three days except in the case of janabah. For the second, if the khuff is removed or most of the foot comes out to the shin area, the mash is nullified; then only the feet need to be washed (the wudu remains). Evidence is from the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: "until he removes them" and from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i's statement: "If you remove them, wash your feet." For the third, if water reaches most of one foot, it effectively becomes washed, so mashing cannot be combined with washing; both khuffs must be removed and both feet washed. This is stated as the correct view. For the fourth, when the permitted period ends (one day for resident, three for traveler), the mash is broken; however, if severe cold threatens the foot, it takes the ruling of a splint (jabirah)—mash continues as long as the excuse lasts. Support comes from the hadith of 'Ali regarding the jabirah. Finally, the text clarifies that after any of the last three nullifiers (removal, water, or expiry), if wudu is still intact, only washing the feet is required, not the entire wudu.

Key Terms
مسح الخف (masah al-khuff): Wiping over the leather socks (khuffs) with wet hands during ablution, a concession granted for travelers and residents within specific time limits.
ساق الخف (saq al-khuff): The upper part of the khuff that extends to the shin area of the leg.
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Anything that invalidates ablution, such as passing wind, urine, stool, blood, or loss of reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT invalidate the mash over khuffs according to this passage?
A) Passing wind or urine
B) Removing the khuff and most of the foot exiting
C) Touching one's spouse with desire
D) Expiry of the time limit (without fear of cold harm)

Key Takeaway
The mash over khuffs is nullified by four specific events; knowing them ensures you maintain a valid state.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Obligation of Prayer
Ruling with proof: defining salah and its conditions for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the obligation of salah in the Hanafi school, cite the Quranic and hadith evidence, and explain why a child's prayer is valid but not obligatory.

Core Idea
Prayer is obligatory only upon a sane adult Muslim; children and the insane are not held accountable.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah defines salah and establishes its obligation using Quran and hadith. It then lists three prerequisites that must be present for salah to be wajib upon an individual. Understanding these conditions (shurut al-wujub) is essential for distinguishing between who must pray and whose prayer is simply rewardable. The Hanafi position is clarified, including the ruling on children and the insane.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions for obligation
State them clearly: Islam, puberty (bulugh), and sanity (aql).
These are conditions for the prayer being obligatory, not for its validity.
2
Distinguish between conditions for obligation and conditions for validity
The conditions listed determine who must pray. A child's prayer is valid (if performed correctly) but not obligatory. An insane person's prayer is not valid because sanity is also needed for intention.
Hanafi fiqh separates shurut al-wujub from shurut al-sihha.
3
Cite the Quranic proof
Surah An-Nisa 4:103: 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers a decree of specified times.' This verse establishes the obligation on believers.
The verse addresses 'believers,' implying Islam is a condition.
4
Cite the hadith proof
The hadith of the Night Journey (Isra') shows how Allah initially imposed fifty prayers, then reduced to five. This demonstrates the obligation of five daily prayers.
The hadith is used to support the fard status of salah.
5
Apply the conditions to specific cases
Practice with scenarios: a non-Muslim, a child under puberty, a sane adult, and an insane person. Determine who is obligated.
Remember: obligation applies only when all three conditions are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة ضروری نوٹ : صلوۃ کے لغوی معنی دعا ہے۔ شریعت میں ارکان معہودہ کو صلوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ صلوۃ کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل قرآن کی بہت سی آیتیں ہیں ۔ مثلا ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۱۰۳ سورۃ النساء۴) (۲) نماز فرض ہونے کی دلیل حدیث میں یہ ہے۔ کان ابو ذر يحدث أن رسول الله الله قال فرج عن سقف بيتى و أنا بمكة ..... قال النبي الله : ففرض الله على امتى خمسين صلاة فرجعت بذالک حتی مررت علی موسی .... قال : هن خمس و هن خمسون ، لا يبدل القول لدى ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف فرضت الصلاة في الاسراء ص ۶۲ نمبر ۳۴۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانچوں نمازیں کیسے فرض ہوئیں نوٹ : نماز اہم عبادت ہے اور طہارت اس کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اس لئے طہارت کو مقدم کیا۔ اب طہارت کے ابحاث ختم ہونے کے بعد نماز کے مسائل کو شروع فرمایا۔ ترجمه : (۲۹۲) نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے تین شرطیں ہیں: ...... اسلام۔ بلوغ اور عقل۔ وجه : کافر پر نماز فرض نہیں ہے صرف مسلمان پر فرض ہے اس لئے نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے پہلی شرط مسلمان ہونا ہے۔ بالغ نہ و اور عقلمند نہ ہو بلکہ بچہ یا مجنون ہو تو اس پر نماز فرض نہیں ہے اس لئے نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے دوسری اور تیسری شرط عاقل و بالغ ہونا ہے۔ اس کے لئے حدیث باب الوضوء میں گزر چکی ہے۔
Book of Prayer. Necessary note: The lexical meaning of salah is supplication. In Shariah, it refers to the specific prescribed actions. The evidence for the obligation of salah is many Quranic verses, e.g., 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers a decree of specified times' (4:103). (2) Evidence for the obligation of salah in hadith: Abu Dharr narrated that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The roof of my house was split open while I was in Mecca...' ... The Prophet said: 'Allah imposed fifty prayers upon my ummah. I returned and passed by Musa... He said: They are five and they are fifty, the word does not change with Me.' (Bukhari, Bab kayfa furidat al-salat fi al-Isra', p. 62, no. 349). This hadith explains how the five prayers became obligatory. Note: Prayer is an important worship and purification is a condition for it. Therefore purification was presented first. Now after the topics of purification are finished, the issues of prayer are begun. Translation: (292) Three things are conditions for the obligation of prayer: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Explanation: Prayer is not obligatory upon a disbeliever, only upon a Muslim. So the first condition is being Muslim. If one is not an adult and not sane, i.e., a child or insane, then prayer is not obligatory upon him. So the second and third conditions are sanity and puberty. The hadith for this has passed in the Chapter of Wudu.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a combination of an introductory note and a ruling on the conditions for the obligation of prayer. The author first defines salah lexically and technically, then provides Quranic and hadith evidence for its obligation. The Quranic verse from Surah Nisa (4:103) is cited, and the hadith of the Night Journey is narrated, showing the obligation of five daily prayers. Then the ruling (292) states that three conditions are required for prayer to be obligatory on a person: Islam, puberty, and sanity. The explanation clarifies that non-Muslims are not obligated, and children and the insane are not obligated. This is the standard Hanafi position. The note also explains why the Book of Purification came before the Book of Prayer: because purification is a condition for prayer. For the conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub), the Hanafi school requires Islam, bulugh, and aql. These are conditions for the prayer being obligatory, not for its validity; a child's prayer is valid but not obligatory.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): In Shariah, it refers to the specific prescribed actions (arkan) for worship; lexically it means supplication.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; an act that is required and its omission is sinful.
البلوغ (al-bulugh): Puberty; the age at which a person becomes legally responsible for religious duties.
العقل (al-aql): Sanity; the ability to understand and be responsible for actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Islam, puberty, and wealth
B) Islam, sanity, and residence
C) Islam, puberty, and sanity
D) Faith, purity, and direction of Qibla

Key Takeaway
The obligation of salah is conditional upon three specific prerequisites: Islam, puberty, and sanity; without any of these, the individual is not legally required to pray.

Commanding Children to Pray: The Ruling at Seven and Ten
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation on guardians to command children to pray at seven and discipline at ten, and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet ﷺ commanded guardians to train children in salah from age seven, and to use light discipline at ten.

This lesson covers the hadith-based obligation on parents and guardians regarding the training of children in prayer. Understanding the ages and the measure of discipline is essential for proper Islamic upbringing. The Hanafi school derives a clear ruling from the imperative in the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the guardian's duty to command the child to pray and to discipline if neglected. The ruling is wajib on the guardian.
The act is not the child's prayer but the guardian's training.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Command the boy to pray when he reaches seven years, and when he reaches ten years, beat him for it.' This is an ahad hadith.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (مروا, اضربوه) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contrary indicator. Thus, the command imposes a duty on guardians.
No contrary indicator exists here, so it is wajib.
4
Note the age distinctions
At seven, the child is to be commanded (verbal instruction). At ten, if neglecting, the guardian may use light beating (ضرب خفيف). The ages are based on the child's ability to understand and start training.
The beating is disciplinary, not punitive, and must be light.
5
Identify conditions and limits
The beating is not absolute; it is a last resort after instruction. It must be non-injurious and proportionate. The obligation applies to both boys and girls, though the hadith mentions 'الصبي'.
Guardians should use wisdom in implementation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۹۳) وتؤمر بها الاولاد لسبع و يضربون عليها لعشر . وجه : عن عبد الملک ابن الربيع... قال قال النبى الله مروا الصبي بالصلاة اذا بلغ سبع سنين واذا بلغ عشر سنين فاضربوه عليها - (ابوداود شریف، باب متى يومر الغلام بالصلاة ، ص ۸۲ نمبر ۴۹۴ مترمذی شریف ، باب ما جا تی یو مر الصحي بالصلاۃ ، ص ۱۰۹، نمبر ۴۰۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سات سال کی عمر میں نماز کا حکم دو ، اور دس سال کی عمر میں ہلکی پھلکی مار مارو۔
(293) And the children are commanded to pray at seven, and they are beaten for it at ten. Evidence: From Abd al-Malik ibn al-Rabi'... that the Prophet said: 'Command the boy to pray when he reaches seven years, and when he reaches ten years, beat him for it.' (Abu Dawood, Chapter of When the Boy is Commanded to Pray, p. 82, no. 494; Tirmidhi, Chapter of Commanding the Child to Pray, p. 109, no. 407). This hadith means that at seven years of age they should be commanded, and at ten years they should be lightly beaten.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the tarbiyah (training) of children regarding salah. The author states that children are to be commanded to pray at the age of seven, and if they neglect it, they should be beaten at the age of ten. The proof is the hadith from Abd al-Malik ibn al-Rabi' that the Prophet commanded guardians to instruct their boys at seven and discipline them at ten. The type of beating is light and non-injurious, as specified in other texts. This ruling is for the guardian (parent or custodian) and is considered wajib based on the imperative in the hadith. In the Hanafi school, training in prayer begins at seven, and more forceful discipline may be used at ten, but with the condition that it is not severe. This is to establish the habit of prayer before the age of obligation (puberty).

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabiyy): A male child before puberty, in this context specifically from age seven to ten.
الضرب (al-darb): Light beating as a disciplinary measure, not severe or injurious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The guardian is obligated by the Prophet's command to train children in prayer from age seven and to use light discipline at ten if needed.

The Meaning of Salah: Linguistic and Technical Definitions
Author defines salah linguistically and technically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the linguistic meaning of salah (supplication) from its technical meaning (prescribed actions) and explain why this distinction matters.

Core Idea
Salah is a defined act with specific actions, not just any prayer.

The term 'salah' is used in both a general linguistic sense and a specific legal sense. The author begins by clarifying this, ensuring that the reader understands that the rulings of salah apply only to the specific ritual prayer defined by the Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
Find where the author states the linguistic meaning (du'ā') and the technical meaning (arkān ma'hūdah).
2
Note the transition
The author moves from general language to Shari'ah definition, showing that fiqh uses precise terms.
3
Understand the practical implication
The technical definition excludes other forms of supplication from the rulings of salah (e.g., conditions, pillars).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
ضروری نوٹ : صلوۃ کے لغوی معنی دعا ہے۔ شریعت میں ارکان معہودہ کو صلوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ صلوۃ کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل قرآن کی بہت سی آیتیں ہیں ۔ مثلا ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۱۰۳ سورۃ النساء۴) (۲) نماز فرض ہونے کی دلیل حدیث میں یہ ہے۔ کان ابو ذر يحدث أن رسول الله الله قال فرج عن سقف بيتى و أنا بمكة ..... قال النبي الله : ففرض الله على امتى خمسين صلاة فرجعت بذالک حتی مررت علی موسی .... قال : هن خمس و هن خمسون ، لا يبدل القول لدى ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف فرضت الصلاة في الاسراء ص ۶۲ نمبر ۳۴۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانچوں نمازیں کیسے فرض ہوئیں
نوٹ : نماز اہم عبادت ہے اور طہارت اس کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اس لئے طہارت کو مقدم کیا۔ اب طہارت کے ابحاث ختم ہونے کے بعد نماز کے مسائل کو شروع فرمایا۔
Book of Prayer. Essential Note: The lexical meaning of 'salah' is supplication. In Shari'ah, it refers to the prescribed actions (arkan). The evidence for the obligation of salah from the Quran includes many verses, such as: 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at fixed times' (Surah an-Nisa 4:103). (2) The evidence for the obligation of salah from hadith is: 'Abu Dharr narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The ceiling of my house was opened while I was in Makkah... The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: So Allah made fifty prayers obligatory upon my Ummah... Then I passed by Musa... He said: They are five and they are fifty; the word with Me does not change.' (Sahih Bukhari, Kitab al-Isra, no. 349). This hadith explains how the five prayers were made obligatory. Note: Salah is an important act of worship, and purification is a condition for it. Therefore, purification was presented first. Now that the discussions on purification have ended, the issues of prayer are commenced.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the Book of Prayer (Kitab as-Salah). He begins by giving the linguistic and technical definitions of salah: linguistically it means supplication, and technically it refers to the specific prescribed actions (arkan) performed in worship. The author then provides evidence for the obligation of salah from both the Quran and Sunnah. From the Quran, he quotes the verse from Surah an-Nisa (4:103) establishing that prayer is decreed upon believers at appointed times. From the Sunnah, he cites the well-known hadith of the Mi'raj in which fifty prayers were initially prescribed and later reduced to five, yet their reward remains as fifty. This hadith is found in Sahih Bukhari. Finally, the author explains why the book on purification preceded this one: purification is a condition for prayer, so it was logical to cover it first. Now, having completed purification, the author begins the actual rulings of salah.

Key Terms
صلوۃ (salah): In this text, salah refers to the specific ritual prayer with its prescribed actions (arkan) as defined by the Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Evidence for the Obligation of Salah
Author presents the evidence for salah's obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and Hadith evidence for the obligation of salah and explain how each proves the ruling.

Core Idea
Salah's obligation is established by both Quran and Sunnah, making it a definitive ruling.

Having defined salah, the author now provides the foundational evidence from the Quran and the Prophet's Sunnah. This establishes the legal basis for one of the most important acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic proof
Locate the verse from Surah an-Nisa (4:103). Note the key phrase 'kitāban mawqūtan' which indicates a fixed obligation.
2
Identify the Hadith proof
The author cites the hadith of Mi'rāj from Sahih Bukhari. Note how it shows the divine command for five prayers.
The hadith mentions fifty prayers reduced to five.
3
Understand the combined force
The Quran gives the principle; the Hadith specifies the number and details. Together they make the obligation clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
ضروری نوٹ : صلوۃ کے لغوی معنی دعا ہے۔ شریعت میں ارکان معہودہ کو صلوۃ کہتے ہیں۔ صلوۃ کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل قرآن کی بہت سی آیتیں ہیں ۔ مثلا ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۱۰۳ سورۃ النساء۴) (۲) نماز فرض ہونے کی دلیل حدیث میں یہ ہے۔ کان ابو ذر يحدث أن رسول الله الله قال فرج عن سقف بيتى و أنا بمكة ..... قال النبي الله : ففرض الله على امتى خمسين صلاة فرجعت بذالک حتی مررت علی موسی .... قال : هن خمس و هن خمسون ، لا يبدل القول لدى ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف فرضت الصلاة في الاسراء ص ۶۲ نمبر ۳۴۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانچوں نمازیں کیسے فرض ہوئیں
نوٹ : نماز اہم عبادت ہے اور طہارت اس کے لئے شرط ہے۔ اس لئے طہارت کو مقدم کیا۔ اب طہارت کے ابحاث ختم ہونے کے بعد نماز کے مسائل کو شروع فرمایا۔
Book of Prayer. Essential Note: The lexical meaning of 'salah' is supplication. In Shari'ah, it refers to the prescribed actions (arkan). The evidence for the obligation of salah from the Quran includes many verses, such as: 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at fixed times' (Surah an-Nisa 4:103). (2) The evidence for the obligation of salah from hadith is: 'Abu Dharr narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The ceiling of my house was opened while I was in Makkah... The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: So Allah made fifty prayers obligatory upon my Ummah... Then I passed by Musa... He said: They are five and they are fifty; the word with Me does not change.' (Sahih Bukhari, Kitab al-Isra, no. 349). This hadith explains how the five prayers were made obligatory. Note: Salah is an important act of worship, and purification is a condition for it. Therefore, purification was presented first. Now that the discussions on purification have ended, the issues of prayer are commenced.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to the Book of Prayer (Kitab as-Salah). He begins by giving the linguistic and technical definitions of salah: linguistically it means supplication, and technically it refers to the specific prescribed actions (arkan) performed in worship. The author then provides evidence for the obligation of salah from both the Quran and Sunnah. From the Quran, he quotes the verse from Surah an-Nisa (4:103) establishing that prayer is decreed upon believers at appointed times. From the Sunnah, he cites the well-known hadith of the Mi'raj in which fifty prayers were initially prescribed and later reduced to five, yet their reward remains as fifty. This hadith is found in Sahih Bukhari. Finally, the author explains why the book on purification preceded this one: purification is a condition for prayer, so it was logical to cover it first. Now, having completed purification, the author begins the actual rulings of salah.

Key Terms
صلوۃ (salah): In this text, salah refers to the specific ritual prayer with its prescribed actions (arkan) as defined by the Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Conditions for Obligation of Salah
Author states the three conditions for the obligation of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the obligation of salah and determine who is exempted from this obligation.

Core Idea
Salah is only obligatory upon a Muslim who has reached puberty and is of sound mind.

This lesson introduces the foundational conditions that trigger the obligation of salah. The author presents three simple but essential requirements: being Muslim, having reached puberty, and possessing intellect. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly identifying who must pray and who is excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is salah (ritual prayer). The ruling is that it is obligatory (fard) upon certain individuals. We need to determine who those individuals are.
The obligation is a fard 'ayn on every eligible person.
2
List the three conditions
The author explicitly states three conditions: Islam, puberty (bulugh), and intellect (aql). Memorize these three.
They are shurut al-wujub (conditions for obligation), not shurut al-sihhah (conditions for validity).
3
Explain the legal effect of each condition
Islam: a non-Muslim is not addressed by the obligation of salah at all. Puberty: a child who has not reached puberty is not obligated, though encouraged. Intellect: an insane person is not obligated.
These conditions are based on the principle of taklif (legal capacity).
4
Identify who is exempt
The exempted categories are: non-Muslims, pre-pubescent children, and the insane. They are not required to pray, but if a child or insane person prays, it is valid.
For the insane, no makeup is required upon recovery.
5
Note the source of these conditions
The author references that the evidence for the obligation of salah from Quran and hadith was already presented earlier. The conditions are derived from the general principle of taklif.
No specific dalil is cited here; it is a matn (text) intended for memorization.

Source Text

(۲۹۲) يشترط لفرضيَّتها ثلاثه اشياء. الاسلام والبلوغ والعقل .
ترجمه : (۲۹۲) نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے تین شرطیں ہیں: اسلام، بلوغ اور عقل۔
وجه : کافر پر نماز فرض نہیں ہے صرف مسلمان پر فرض ہے اس لئے نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے پہلی شرط مسلمان ہونا ہے۔ بالغ نہ و اور عقلمند نہ ہو بلکہ بچہ یا مجنون ہو تو اس پر نماز فرض نہیں ہے اس لئے نماز فرض ہونے کے لئے دوسری اور تیسری شرط عاقل و بالغ ہونا ہے۔
(292) Three things are conditions for its obligation: Islam, puberty, and intellect. Translation: For salah to be obligatory, three conditions: Islam, puberty, and intellect. Explanation: Salah is not obligatory upon a disbeliever; it is only obligatory upon a Muslim. Hence the first condition is being Muslim. If one has not reached puberty or is not sane, i.e., a child or an insane person, then salah is not obligatory upon him. Thus the second and third conditions are sanity and puberty.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is a ruling statement (matn) listing the three conditions for the obligation (fardiyyah) of salah. The author states that for salah to become an obligatory duty on a person, three conditions must be met: being Muslim, having reached puberty, and being of sound mind. The explanation clarifies: a non-Muslim is not addressed by the obligation of salah at all; that is the condition of Islam. A child who has not reached puberty is not obligated, nor is an insane person who lacks intellect. These conditions are based on the general principle that legal responsibility (taklif) requires the ability to understand and comply. The author also references that the hadith evidence for the obligation of salah upon the believer has already been mentioned in the chapter on wudu.

Key Terms
فرضیَّت (fardiyyah): The state of being obligatory; in this context it refers to the obligation of the salah upon an individual.
بلوغ (bulugh): Reaching puberty, the age at which a person becomes legally responsible for performing religious duties.
عقل (aql): Intellect or sanity; a person who lacks aql (insane) is not held accountable for obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Salah — Prayer

Causes of Salah and Expanded Obligation
Explanation of the cause of salah and expanded obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the cause of salah is its time and explain the concept of wujub musawwa' (expanded obligation).

Core Idea
The time of salah is its cause; obligation begins immediately but expands across the entire period.

In this passage, the author explains the fundamental link between prayer times and the obligation of salah. You will learn that although salah becomes obligatory as soon as its time enters, you are not required to pray immediately—you may perform it at any point within that time window. This concept is called wujub musawwa', and it is supported by both the Quran and the well-known hadith of Jibril's leadership in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its cause
Read the first part: 'And their causes are their times.' Recognize that the sabab (cause) for the obligation of salah is the entry of its designated time. Note the Quranic evidence: 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at fixed times' (4:103).
The cause is not the command itself but the time that signals the command.
2
Understand the nature of the obligation
The next part: 'It becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with an expanded obligation.' This means the obligation (wujub) attaches at the very start of the time, but it is musawwa' (expanded)—you may pray at any moment within the entire time span without incurring sin or making it qada.
Contrast with wujub mudayyaq (immediate obligation), e.g., fasting in Ramadan.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith of Jibril praying with the Prophet at the Kaaba twice establishes the earliest and latest times for each prayer. On the first day, Jibril prayed each salah at its earliest time; on the second day, at its latest time. This demonstrates the valid range.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud; its thubut is qati' (mutawatir) and dalala is zanni (interpretive).
4
Apply the concept to a scenario
Consider Dhuhr time: from when the sun passes the zenith (zawal) until the shadow of an object becomes twice its length (according to Hanafi). The obligation begins at zawal, but you can pray at any point until the end of Dhuhr time.
This expansion is unique to salah; other acts like fasting are mudayyaq.

Source Text

(۲۹۴) واسبابها اوقاتها. (۲۹۵) وتجب باول الوقت وجوبا موسعا .
ترجمه : (۲۹۴) اور نماز کے اسباب ان کے اوقات ہیں۔
تشریح : نماز اصل میں اللہ کے حکم سے واجب ہوتی ہے، لیکن انسان اللہ کے حکم کو نہیں سن سکتا ہے اس لئے وقت کو اس کا سبب قرار دیا کہ جب وقت آ جائے تو سمجھو کہ اللہ کا حکم آگیا۔
وجه : اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز وقت کے ساتھ متعین ہے، اس لئے وقت نماز کے لئے سبب ہوا۔ ان الصلوة كانت على المؤمنين كتابا موقوتا. (آیت ۱۰۳، سورۃ النساء ۴)
ترجمه : (۲۹۵) اول وقت میں نماز واجب ہوتی ہے لیکن گنجائش ہے کہ پورے وقت میں سے کسی وقت بھی ادا کر لے۔ تشریح : وقت نماز کا سبب ہے اس لئے جیسے ہی وقت شروع ہوا نماز واجب ہوگئی لیکن پورے وقت میں جب بھی ادا کرے گا قضا شمار نہیں کی جائے گی ادا ہی ہوگی ، کیونکہ اس وقت میں گنجائش ہے کہ وقت کے کسی حصے میں ادا کر لے ۔ اس کو, وجو با موسعا، کہتے ہیں۔
وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ اخبرني ابن عباس ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين فصلى الظهر في الأولى منهما حين كان الفيء مثل الشراك ثم صلى العصر حين كان كل شيء مثل ظله ثم صلى المغرب حين وجبت الشمس وافطر الصائم ثم صلى العشاء حين غاب الشفق ثم صلى الفجر حين برق الفجر وحرم الطعام على الصائم وصلى المرة الثانية الظهر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثله لوقت العصر بالامس ثم صلى العصر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثليه ثم صلى المغرب لوقته الاول ثم صلى العشاء الآخرة حين ذهب ثلث الليل ثم صلى الصبح حين اسفرت الارض ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء مواقیت الصلوة عن النبي الا الله ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب المواقیت ، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے دن تمام نمازیں اول وقت میں پڑھیں ، اور چونکہ آخر وقت میں پڑھنے کی گنجائش ہے اس لئے دوسرے دن تمام نمازیں آخر وقت میں پڑھیں۔ اور پانچوں نمازوں کے اول وقت اور آخر وقت کا بھی ثبوت ہوا۔
(294) And their causes are their times. (295) And it becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with a fully expanded obligation. Translation: The causes of salah are its times. (295) It becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with an expanded obligation (that allows performance at any point within that time). Explanation: Prayer is originally made obligatory by Allah's command, but since man cannot directly hear Allah's command, the time is designated as its cause. So when the time enters, one knows that Allah's command has come. Evidence: The verse says: 'Indeed, prayer has been decreed upon the believers at fixed times' (Surah an-Nisa 4:103). Thus time is the cause. (295) The obligation sets in at the beginning of the time, but there is leeway to perform it at any time within the entire period. Whichever part of the time one prays, it counts as ada (timely performance), not qada (makeup), because of the expanded scope. This is called wujub musawwa'. Evidence: The hadith: Ibn Abbas narrated that Jibril led the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer twice at the Kaaba... Then Jibril turned and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times. (Tirmidhi, no. 149; Abu Dawud, no. 393). The hadith shows that the first day all prayers were prayed at the beginning of their times, and the second day at the end, indicating the expanded range.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage explains the relationship between the times of prayer and their obligation. The author states two rulings: (294) the cause (sabab) of salah is its designated time. Salah is made obligatory by Allah's command, but for humans the time serves as the tangible indicator of when the obligation is in effect. The Quranic verse (4:103) supports that prayer is tied to specific times. (295) The obligation of salah begins at the very start of its time (awwal al-waqt), but it is an expanded obligation (wujub musawwa'), meaning that one may perform it at any point during the entire time period without it being considered late (qada). This is because the time is the cause, and once the cause exists, the obligation is immediate, but it does not require immediate performance; it can be delayed within the time without sin. The author then provides a lengthy hadith in which Jibril led the Prophet in prayer at the beginning of each time on one day and at the end of each time on the next day, illustrating the boundaries (first and last times) of each prayer. This hadith is from Sahih texts like Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud. The author concludes that the first and last times for all five prayers are established through this hadith.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation of salah; here it is the entry of time.
وجوب موسع (wujub musawwa'): An expanded obligation that becomes binding immediately but allows performance at any point within the time span.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Salah's obligation is tied to its time; it begins at the start but is expanded so that any performance within the entire time counts as ada.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
The Cause of Prayer and Expansive Obligation
States the cause of prayer is its time and the obligation is expansive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sabab (cause) of prayer in Hanafi fiqh and explain the concept of wujub muwassa' (expansive obligation) with its proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Time is the cause of prayer; the obligation is expansive – you may pray at any point within the time.

In Hanafi fiqh, prayer becomes obligatory not by a direct audible command, but through the arrival of its prescribed time. This time serves as the legal cause (sabab). Furthermore, the Hanafi school teaches that this obligation is expansive (wujub muwassa'): once the time enters, the prayer is due, but you may perform it at any moment within the entire time window without being sinful for delaying. This unique understanding is supported by the Quran and the famous hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer at both the earliest and latest permissible times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the cause of prayer
Read the passage's first statement: 'Its causes are its times.' Understand that the sabab (legal cause) triggering the obligation of prayer is the arrival of its prescribed time, not a direct command from Allah.
The Urdu commentary clarifies that time is made the cause because humans cannot perceive Allah's command directly.
2
Locate the Quranic proof for time as cause
The passage cites Quran 4:103: 'Indeed prayer has been a prescribed duty upon the believers at appointed times.' The term 'mawqoota' (appointed times) shows that prayer is tied to specific times, establishing time as the cause.
This proof is qat'i al-thubut from the Quran.
3
Locate the hadith proof for expansive obligation
The hadith of Jibril records the Prophet praying each of the five prayers at the earliest time on one day and at the latest time on another day. This demonstrates that the valid time for each prayer spans from its beginning to its end.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for establishing the ruling in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand wujub muwassa' vs. fawr
The Hanafi school holds that the obligation is expansive (muwassa'): as soon as the time begins, the prayer becomes wajib, but the worshiper may perform it at any point within the time. If done within the time, it counts as ada (on time), not qada (missed). Some other schools hold that the obligation is immediate (fawr), i.e., must be prayed as soon as time enters.
This difference leads to a practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, delaying prayer within its time without excuse is not sinful, whereas in the Shafi'i school it would be sinful.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who delays Zuhr prayer until just before Asr enters. According to Hanafi fiqh, the prayer is ada and valid, and the person is not sinful. This is because the obligation is expansive.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is whether delay is permitted without sin.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Thamaratun Najah Volume 1, page 206, Book of Prayer. (294) And its causes are its times. (295) And it becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with expansive obligation. Translation: (294) The causes of prayer are its times. Explanation: Prayer is originally obligatory by Allah's command, but humans cannot hear Allah's command, so the time is made its cause: when the time comes, understand that Allah's command has come. Proof: This verse states that prayer is fixed with time, therefore time is the cause for prayer. 'Indeed prayer has been a prescribed duty upon the believers at appointed times.' (Surah An-Nisa 4:103) Translation: (295) Prayer becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time, but there is leeway to perform it at any time within the whole time. Explanation: Time is the cause of prayer, so as soon as the time begins, prayer becomes obligatory, but whenever he performs it within the whole time, it will not be considered qada (missed); it will be ada (on time), because there is leeway in that time to perform it at any part of the time. This is called 'wujub muwassa' (expansive obligation). Proof: This hadith proves it. Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice. He prayed Zuhr in the first time when the shadow was like the strap of a sandal, then Asr when the shadow of everything was like its own, then Maghrib when the sun set and the fasting person breaks fast, then Isha when the twilight disappeared, then Fajr when dawn broke and food was forbidden for the fasting person. In the second time, he prayed Zuhr when the shadow of everything was like its own (like Asr time the previous day), then Asr when the shadow of everything was twice its length, then Maghrib at its first time, then Isha when one-third of the night had passed, then Fajr when the earth became bright. Then he turned to Jibril and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times.' (Tirmidhi, Chapter on Prayer Times from the Prophet, p.42, no.149; Abu Dawud, Chapter on Prayer Times, p.68, no.393) This hadith indicates that on the first day all prayers were performed at the beginning of their times, and since there is leeway to pray at the end, on the second day all prayers were performed at the end of their times. And the beginning and end times for the five prayers are also established.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the cause (sabab) of prayer and the nature of its obligation. The author states that the cause of prayer is its time (284), and that prayer becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time with an expansive obligation (wujub muwassa') (285). The Urdu commentary explains that although prayer is ultimately obligatory by Allah's command, humans cannot directly perceive that command, so the time serves as a tangible indicator that the command has arrived. The proof for time being the cause is the Quranic verse from Surah An-Nisa (4:103): 'Indeed prayer has been a prescribed duty upon the believers at appointed times.' The term 'mawqoota' (appointed times) shows that prayer is tied to specific times, making time its cause. The expansive obligation means that as soon as the time starts, the obligation is triggered, but the worshiper may perform the prayer at any point within the entire time window; if done within the time, it counts as ada (on time), not qada (missed). The proof for this expansive obligation is the famous hadith of Jibril (Gabriel) leading the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer twice at the Kaaba. On the first day, Jibril prayed each prayer at the earliest permissible time, and on the second day, he prayed each prayer at the latest permissible time. This shows that the valid time spans from the beginning to the end. The hadith also establishes the specific beginning and end times for each of the five daily prayers. The author follows the order of the matn: first stating the ruling (cause and expansive obligation), then providing proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): Cause or means; here specifically the time being the legal cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation of prayer.
وجوب موسع (wujub muwassa'): Expansive obligation: an obligation that becomes due at the beginning of its time but can be performed at any point within that time without delay penalty.
وقت (waqt): The prescribed time period for a prayer, which serves as the cause of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer?
A) The command of Allah directly
B) The arrival of the prayer time
C) The adhan (call to prayer)
D) The intention of the worshiper

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the time of prayer is its legal cause, and the obligation is expansive, allowing performance at any point within the time window.

The Five Obligatory Prayer Times and Their Quranic Evidence
Lists the five prayer times and provides Quranic proofs for each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five obligatory prayer times and identify the Quranic verses that establish each time.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly defines the boundaries for each daily prayer, anchoring worship in divine revelation.

In this passage, the author lists the five prayer times: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. The author then cites three Quranic verses that collectively provide proof for all five times. This lesson unpacks those verses and shows how Hanafi scholars derive the prayer times from them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five prayer times
List the five times as stated in the passage: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha.
These are the same times mentioned in the hadith of Jibril.
2
Analyze the first Quranic proof
Examine Surah Ta-Ha 20:130: '...before sunrise, before sunset, during hours of the night, and at the ends of the day.' Map each phrase to a prayer time.
Before sunrise = Fajr; before sunset = Asr; night hours = Maghrib & Isha; ends of day = Zuhr.
3
Analyze the second Quranic proof
Examine Surah Al-Isra 17:78: '...at the decline of the sun until darkness of the night and the Quran at dawn.'
Decline of sun = Zuhr; darkness of night = Isha; Quran at dawn = Fajr.
4
Analyze the third Quranic proof
Examine Surah Al-Baqarah 2:238: 'Guard... the middle prayer.' Identify which prayer is the middle prayer according to Hanafis.
The middle prayer is Asr.
5
Summarize the proof structure
Understand that each prayer time is derived from a composite of Quranic verses, not from a single source.
This demonstrates the systematic nature of Hanafi istinbat.

Thamaratun Najah Volume 1, page 207. The times of prayer. And the times are five. (296) The time of Subh is from the rising of the true dawn until just before sunrise. And there are five prayer times: Explanation: From the previous hadith it became clear that the prayer times are five: [1] Fajr, (2) Zuhr, (3) Asr, [4] Maghrib, [5] Isha. Their details are coming ahead. Proof: (1) All prayer times are in this verse: 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting, and during the hours of the night glorify, and at the ends of the day, that you may be pleased.' (Surah Ta-Ha 20:130). 'Before the rising of the sun' provides proof for Fajr prayer, 'before its setting' for Asr, 'hours of the night' for Maghrib and Isha, and 'ends of the day' for Zuhr prayer. (2) 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun until the darkness of the night and (recite) the Quran at dawn.' (Surah Al-Isra 17:78). In this verse, 'decline of the sun' proves Zuhr, 'darkness of the night' proves Isha, and 'Quran at dawn' proves Fajr. (3) 'Guard strictly the prayers, and the middle prayer.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:238). In this, 'middle prayer' proves Asr. Note: For the whole world, the prayer times (like first and second times, the times for 18 degrees, 7.5 degrees, 15 degrees, 120 degrees, sunrise, sunset) are all available at www.nao.rl.ac.uk. Set the longitude and latitude of your city and take the times for the whole year. Inside this website, there is websurf, where all times of the moon and sun are found. Translation: (296) [1] The time of Subh is from the rising of the true dawn (subh sadiq) until just before sunrise. Explanation: Dawn has two types: (1) false dawn (subh kadhib) and (2) true dawn (subh sadiq). False dawn is an elongated light like the tail of a wolf on the eastern horizon, which is very hard to see. In hadith it is called 'fajr mustatil' (elongated dawn). After a short while, there is a spread-out light in an arched shape, which is called 'fajr munhatir' or 'subh sadiq' (true dawn). Some astronomers say it is at 18 degrees and some at 15 degrees. There are proofs on both sides. At the time of this true dawn, Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. Proof: (1) Its evidence is in this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not be deceived by the adhan of Bilal nor by the elongated whiteness of the horizon like this, until it spreads like this.' (Muslim, Book of Fasting, chapter on the entry into fasting occurring with the rising of dawn, p.446, no.2546/1094; Abu Dawud, chapter on the time of suhur, p.1341, no.2346; Tirmidhi, chapter on the clarification of dawn, p.179, no.705). From the hadith it became clear that the light which is elongated is not the true dawn.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the five prayer times, with detailed focus on the time of Fajr. It begins by stating that the prayer times are five (296) and then lists them: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha. The commentary notes that the previous hadith of Jibril already indicated the number of times. The author then provides three Quranic proofs for the times: (1) Surah Ta-Ha (20:130) which mentions glorification before sunrise, before sunset, during the night, and at the ends of the day, corresponding to Fajr, Asr, Maghrib/Isha, and Zuhr respectively. (2) Surah Al-Isra (17:78) which mentions the decline of the sun (Zuhr), darkness of the night (Isha), and the dawn recitation (Fajr). (3) Surah Al-Baqarah (2:238) which commands guarding the prayers especially the middle prayer, identified as Asr. A modern note explains that prayer times can be calculated based on astronomical data. Next, the passage gives the ruling for Fajr specifically: its time is from the rising of the true dawn (subh sadiq) until just before sunrise. The Urdu commentary explains the two types of dawn: false dawn (subh kadhib) which is an elongated light on the horizon, and true dawn (subh sadiq) which is a spreading light in an arched shape. The true dawn is the basis for Fajr obligation, and astronomers estimate it at 18 or 15 degrees below the horizon. The proof is the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub, which warns against being misled by the elongated false dawn, affirming that true dawn is the spreading light.

Key Terms
فجر (fajr): The dawn; the time for the first daily prayer, beginning at true dawn.
ظهر (zuhr): The noon prayer; begins after the sun passes its zenith (zawal).
عصر (asr): The afternoon prayer; begins when the shadow of an object equals its height (according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) or twice its height (Muhammad).
مغرب (maghrib): The evening prayer; begins immediately after sunset.
عشاء (isha): The night prayer; begins after the disappearance of the evening twilight (shafaq).
صلاة الوسطى (salat al-wusta): The middle prayer, understood by Hanafis to be the Asr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many prayer times are there according to the passage?
A) 3
B) 4
C) 5
D) 7

Key Takeaway
The Quran, through a combination of verses, provides clear evidence for the five daily prayer times, each mapped to a specific celestial event.

The Time of Fajr: True Dawn vs False Dawn
Explains the two types of dawn and the hadith that establishes the time for Fajr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between false dawn (subh kadhib) and true dawn (subh sadiq) and state the ruling that Fajr prayer begins at true dawn.

Core Idea
The hadith of Samurah draws a clear dividing line: Fajr begins at the spreading light, not at the false dawn's vertical streak.

The passage distinguishes two types of dawn: the false dawn, which appears as an elongated vertical light, and the true dawn, which spreads horizontally. The hadith of Samurah explicitly warns against being deceived by the false dawn and confirms that the true dawn marks the start of Fajr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of dawn
Name the two dawns: false dawn (subh kadhib) and true dawn (subh sadiq).
The false dawn is also called fajr mustatil (elongated dawn).
2
Describe their visual characteristics
The false dawn is a vertical column of light like a wolf's tail. The true dawn is a horizontal spread of light across the horizon.
The true dawn appears after the false dawn has dissipated.
3
Read the hadith of Samurah
Understand the warning: do not be deceived by the elongated whiteness; wait for the spreading light.
The hadith is authenticated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
4
Connect the hadith to the ruling
The ruling: Fajr time begins only at true dawn. Praying before that is invalid.
This is agreed upon by all madhahib.
5
Note the astronomical measurement
Some astronomers set the angle at 18°, others at 15°. Both are valid approximations; the actual observation is the criterion.
In regions where observation is difficult, calculation may be used.

Translation: (296) [1] The time of Subh is from the rising of the true dawn (subh sadiq) until just before sunrise. Explanation: Dawn has two types: (1) false dawn (subh kadhib) and (2) true dawn (subh sadiq). False dawn is an elongated light like the tail of a wolf on the eastern horizon, which is very hard to see. In hadith it is called 'fajr mustatil' (elongated dawn). After a short while, there is a spread-out light in an arched shape, which is called 'fajr munhatir' or 'subh sadiq' (true dawn). Some astronomers say it is at 18 degrees and some at 15 degrees. There are proofs on both sides. At the time of this true dawn, Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. Proof: (1) Its evidence is in this hadith: From Samurah ibn Jundub, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not be deceived by the adhan of Bilal nor by the elongated whiteness of the horizon like this, until it spreads like this.' (Muslim, Book of Fasting, chapter on the entry into fasting occurring with the rising of dawn, p.446, no.2546/1094; Abu Dawud, chapter on the time of suhur, p.1341, no.2346; Tirmidhi, chapter on the clarification of dawn, p.179, no.705). From the hadith it became clear that the light which is elongated is not the true dawn.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the five prayer times, with detailed focus on the time of Fajr. It begins by stating that the prayer times are five (296) and then lists them: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha. The commentary notes that the previous hadith of Jibril already indicated the number of times. The author then provides three Quranic proofs for the times: (1) Surah Ta-Ha (20:130) which mentions glorification before sunrise, before sunset, during the night, and at the ends of the day, corresponding to Fajr, Asr, Maghrib/Isha, and Zuhr respectively. (2) Surah Al-Isra (17:78) which mentions the decline of the sun (Zuhr), darkness of the night (Isha), and the dawn recitation (Fajr). (3) Surah Al-Baqarah (2:238) which commands guarding the prayers especially the middle prayer, identified as Asr. A modern note explains that prayer times can be calculated based on astronomical data. Next, the passage gives the ruling for Fajr specifically: its time is from the rising of the true dawn (subh sadiq) until just before sunrise. The Urdu commentary explains the two types of dawn: false dawn (subh kadhib) which is an elongated light on the horizon, and true dawn (subh sadiq) which is a spreading light in an arched shape. The true dawn is the basis for Fajr obligation, and astronomers estimate it at 18 or 15 degrees below the horizon. The proof is the hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub, which warns against being misled by the elongated false dawn, affirming that true dawn is the spreading light.

Key Terms
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): The true dawn: a spreading, arched light on the eastern horizon that signals the beginning of Fajr prayer time.
صبح كاذب (subh kadhib): The false dawn: an elongated, vertical streak of light on the horizon that appears before true dawn and does not count for Fajr.
فجر مستطيل (fajr mustatil): Another name for false dawn, emphasizing its elongated shape.
فجر مستطير (fajr mustatir): Another name for true dawn, emphasizing its spreading nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) An elongated light like a wolf's tail on the horizon
B) A spread-out, arched light on the eastern horizon
C) The adhan of Bilal
D) The disappearance of all stars

Key Takeaway
Fajr prayer time begins only at the true dawn (subh sadiq), a spreading horizontal light, and not at the false dawn (subh kadhib).

The Five Prayer Times and Their Qur'anic Proofs
Introducing the five daily prayer times with Qur'anic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five daily prayer times and identify the Qur'anic verses that prove each one.

Core Idea
The five prayer times are established by clear Qur'anic texts, each verse marking a specific boundary.

This lesson introduces the five obligatory prayer times in Islam: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. You will learn how each time is derived directly from the Qur'an, using three key verses. Understanding the scriptural basis for prayer times is essential for every Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five prayer times
From the passage, list the five prayer times in order: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha. Note that the source mentions 'five' and then labels them.
The times are given in the opening sentence.
2
Locate the first Qur'anic proof (20:130)
Find the verse from Surah Taha. Explain how each phrase corresponds to a prayer: 'before sunrise' = Fajr, 'before sunset' = Asr, 'parts of the night' = Maghrib and Isha, 'ends of the day' = Zuhr.
This single verse covers all five times implicitly.
3
Locate the second proof (17:78)
Identify the verse from Surah al-Isra. 'Decline of the sun' points to Zuhr, 'darkness of the night' to Isha, 'Qur'an at dawn' to Fajr.
Asr is not mentioned here; it is taken from another verse.
4
Locate the third proof (2:238)
Find the verse from Surah al-Baqarah. 'The middle prayer' is interpreted by Hanafi scholars as Asr, completing the set.
This verse also emphasizes guarding all prayers.
5
Synthesize the proofs
Combine all three verses to see that each prayer time has at least one direct Qur'anic reference. Note that the Hanafi school uses these verses as the primary evidence for the obligation of each prayer at its specific time.
The proofs are all from the Qur'an (dalil naqli) and are considered zanni in dalala (interpretation) but qati in thubut (transmission).

The times of prayer are five: (296) The time of Fajr is from the rising of the true dawn until shortly before sunrise. And the prayers have five times: Explanation: From the previous hadith it became known that the times of prayers are five: [1] Fajr (2) Zuhr (3) Asr [4] Maghrib [5] Isha. Their details are coming ahead. Evidence: (1) All the prayer times are in this verse: 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting, and during part of the night glorify Him, and at the ends of the day, that you may be satisfied.' (Surah Taha, 20:130) Before the rising of the sun proves Fajr prayer, before its setting proves Asr prayer, during part of the night proves Maghrib and Isha prayer, and at the ends of the day proves Zuhr prayer. (2) 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun until the darkness of the night and the Qur'an at dawn.' (Surah al-Isra, 17:78) In this verse, the decline of the sun proves Zuhr, the darkness of the night proves Isha, and the Qur'an at dawn proves Fajr. (3) 'Guard strictly the prayers, and the middle prayer.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:238) In this, the middle prayer proves Asr. Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement introducing the five daily prayer times and providing their Qur'anic proofs. The author first states that there are five prayer times (Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha) and then cites three verses from the Qur'an to establish each time. The first verse (20:130) is used to derive Fajr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Zuhr. The second verse (17:78) establishes Zuhr, Isha, and Fajr explicitly. The third verse (2:238) is used to prove Asr as the middle prayer. The note at the end is a practical contemporary addition referring to an online resource for calculating prayer times based on degrees and location, which is not part of the classical fiqh text but is included for convenience. The lesson is purely evidential (dalil naqli) without detailed legal reasoning.

Key Terms
فجر (Fajr): The dawn prayer, performed from true dawn until sunrise.
ظہر (Zuhr): The midday prayer, performed from decline of sun until object's shadow becomes twice its height.
عصر (Asr): The afternoon prayer, performed from when shadow equals twice the object until sunset.
مغرب (Maghrib): The sunset prayer, performed immediately after sunset.
عشاء (Isha): The night prayer, performed after twilight has disappeared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The five daily prayer times are directly established by three Qur'anic verses, and understanding their derivation is essential for correct observance of salah.

Time of Fajr Prayer and Types of Dawn
Expounding Fajr time with definition of true dawn and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and false dawn (al-fajr al-kadhib) and state the ruling for the start of Fajr prayer with its proof from hadith and Quran.

Core Idea
Fajr prayer time begins with the true dawn that spreads horizontally, not the false vertical dawn.

In this lesson, we examine the specific timing of the Fajr prayer, a ruling that depends on accurately identifying the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq). The author provides both a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ and a Quranic verse to confirm the criterion. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct prayer timing and fasting.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for Fajr time
The author begins by stating that Fajr time is from true dawn until just before sunrise. Identify the start and end points.
This is the fundamental ruling (hukm) of the passage.
2
Define the two types of dawn
Learn the features of false dawn (vertical, wolf's tail-like) and true dawn (horizontal spread). Recognize that only true dawn triggers Fajr obligation.
The Arabic terms: فجر كاذب (false) and فجر صادق (true).
3
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub. The Prophet said: 'Do not let the whiteness on the horizon that is elongated deceive you... until it spreads out like this.' The word 'yastatir' (spreads) is the key indicator of true dawn.
This hadith is a dalil naqli from Sunnah ahad, with zanni thubut but qati dalalah.
4
Connect the Quranic verse
The Quran (2:187) says: 'until the white thread becomes distinct from the black thread of dawn.' The word 'tabayyana' (becomes distinct) implies clear visibility, which aligns with the spreading light of true dawn.
This reinforces the hadith and provides a second proof.

Translation: (296) [1] The time of Fajr is from the rising of the true dawn until before sunrise. Explanation: Fajr has two types: (1) False dawn, (2) True dawn. False dawn: It is a long, wolf's tail-like light on the eastern horizon which is very difficult to see. In hadith it is called al-fajr al-mustatil (elongated dawn). It is called false dawn. Shortly after it, there is a light spread in an arch shape, which is called fajr muntashir (spread dawn) and true dawn. Some astronomers say it is at 18 degrees, some at 15 degrees. There are proofs on both sides. At the time of this true dawn, Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. Evidence: (1) Its proof in hadith is: From Samurah ibn Jundub, who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not let the adhan of Bilal or the horizontal whiteness on the horizon deceive you regarding your suhur. Rather, it is like this until it spreads out like this.' [Muslim, Bab Bayan anna al-dukhul fi al-sawm yahsilu bi tulu' al-fajr, Kitab al-Sawm, p. 446, no. 2546/1094; Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt al-Suhur, p. 1341, no. 2346; Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a fi Bayan al-Fajr, p. 179, no. 705] From the hadith it became clear that the light which is in length is not true dawn, but the light that spreads (yastatir) i.e., spreads across the horizon is true dawn. (2) The Quran also indicates this: 'And eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187) 'Tabayyana' (becomes distinct) means the dawn becomes very clear, which occurs at the time of true dawn.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Fajr prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: Fajr time is from true dawn until just before sunrise. He then explains the difference between false dawn (al-fajr al-kadhib) and true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq). False dawn appears as a vertical column of light on the horizon, while true dawn spreads horizontally. The author provides two proofs: (1) A hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub where the Prophet (peace be upon him) distinguishes between the 'horizontal whiteness' (false) and the 'spreading whiteness' (true). (2) A verse from the Quran (2:187) that uses the word 'tabayyana' (becomes distinct), indicating clear visibility which corresponds to true dawn. The Hanafi position is that Fajr prayer becomes obligatory only after true dawn is certain. The passage also notes a difference among astronomers regarding the precise degree of the sun's depression (15 or 18 degrees), but this is a modern observation and does not affect the fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): The true dawn, a horizontal spread of light on the eastern horizon indicating the start of Fajr time.
صبح کاذب (subh kadhib): The false dawn, a vertical column of light that appears before true dawn; does not start Fajr time.
