Zuhr End Time: The Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf over Zuhr end time with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the end time of Zuhr, identify the primary dalil for each, and evaluate the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
Zuhr time: until one shadow or two? A Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences for the muqtadi.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute over the end time of Zuhr prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), held different views based on different hadith evidence. Understanding this ikhtilaf not only sharpens your dalil analysis but affects the validity of a Zuhr prayer offered after one shadow. We will walk through the proofs and see which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed start time
All Hanafi imams agree that Zuhr begins at zawal (sun's decline). Confirm from the hadith of Anas.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr time extends until the shadow of an object becomes twice its height (excluding midday shadow). His primary dalil is the hadith of Abu Dhar where the Prophet delayed Zuhr until the shadow of hillocks appeared.
The delay beyond one shadow is inferred because hillocks only cast visible shadows after the sun is well past the meridian.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and evidence
The Sahibayn hold that Zuhr time ends when the shadow equals the object's height (once). Their key dalil is the hadith of Jibril's imamate, where Jibril prayed Zuhr at the beginning of its time (shadow like a sandal strap).
The Jibril hadith is seen as defining the optimal time, but the Sahibayn interpret it as the limit.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If one delays Zuhr until the shadow is between one and two times, according to Abu Hanifa it is still valid; according to the Sahibayn, the time has expired and the prayer must be made up as qada.
This affects both individual prayer and congregational timings.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Most later Hanafi texts (e.g., Hidayah) rely on Abu Hanifa's view (two shadows). However, Imam Tahawi adopted the Sahibayn's view. The mufta bihi today, especially in the Indian subcontinent, is often Abu Hanifa's, but the Sahibayn view is also given weight in some contexts.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in Hidayah sides with Abu Hanifa; Tahawi (Ikhtilaf al-Fuqaha) favours Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه (٢٩٧) [٢] ظہر کا وقت سورج کے ڈھلنے سے لیکر ہر چیز کا سایہ دوشل ہو جائے یا ایک مثل ہو جائے ۔ استواء کے وقت کے سایہ کے علاوہ ۔ اور دوسرے قول کو یعنی ایک مثل تک ظہر کا وقت رہتا ہے) کو امام طحاوی نے اختیار کیا یہی قول صاحبین کا ہے تشریح : سورج نصف النہار پر آجائے اور اس سے ذرا سا ڈھل جائے اس کو زوال شمس، کہتے ہیں، وہاں سے ظہر کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے، اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دومشل تک رہتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک مثل تک رہتا ہے ۔ اس کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی کو امام طحاوی نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ وجه : (1) امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي ذر قال كنا مع رسول الله الله في سفر فاراد المؤذن صلى الله عليه ان يؤذن للظهر فقال النبي عل ،ابرد، ثم اراد ان يؤذن فقال له ابرد ، حتى رأينا فيء التلول فقال النبي علي ان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم فاذا اشتد الحر فابردوا بالصلوة . (بخاری شریف ، باب الا براد بالظهر في السفر ، ص ٩١ ، نمبر ۵٣٩ ابوداود شریف ، باب وقت صلاة الظهر ص٧٠ نمبر (۴٠) ٹیلہ پستہ قد ہوتا ہے اس کا سایہ نیچے نظر آنے لگے یہ اسی وقت ہوسکتا ہے جب ہر چیز کا سایہ ایک مثل سے زیادہ ہو چکا ہو۔ اس سے اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز ایک مثل کے بعد پڑھی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے ظہر کا وقت دو مثل تک ہے۔ (٢) عن عبد الله بن عمر أنهما حدثاه عن رسول الله له أنه قال : اذا اشتد الحر فابردوا بالصلوة ، فان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم . (بخاری شریف ، باب الا براد بالظهر في شدة الحرص ٩٠، نمبر ۵٣٣ را بو داود شریف ، باب وقت صلاة الظهر ،٧٠ نمبر ۴٠٢) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ گرمی میں ظہر کی تاخیر کی ، اس سے اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز دوشل پر پڑھی ہوگی کیونکہ عرب میں دوشل تک گرمی رہتی ہے۔ (٣) اور دونوں کے یہاں ظہر کا وقت زوال سے شروع ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج حين زاغت الشمس فصلى الظهر. ( بخاری شریف ، باب وقت الظهر عند الزوال ص سے لے نمبر ۵۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج ڈھلتے ہی ظہر کا وقت شروع ہو جاتا ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل امامت جبرئیل والی حدیث ہے۔ اخبرني ابن عباس ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين فصلى الظهر فى الاولى منهما حين كان الفيء مثل الشراك ثم صلى العصر حين كان كل شيء مثل
Translation (297) [2] The time of Zuhr is from the decline of the sun until the shadow of everything becomes twice its height, or until it becomes one time its height, excluding the shadow at midday. And the second saying (that the time of Zuhr remains until one shadow) was adopted by Imam Tahawi; this is the saying of the Sahibayn. Explanation: When the sun reaches the meridian and then declines slightly, that is called zawal (decline). From there the time of Zuhr begins, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa it lasts until twice the shadow. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it lasts until one shadow. After that, the time of Asr begins. Imam Tahawi adopted this. Evidence: (1) The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is this hadith: From Abu Dhar who said: We were with the Messenger of Allah on a journey, and the mu'adhdhin wanted to call the adhan for Zuhr. The Prophet said, 'Make it cool,' then he wanted to call the adhan and he said, 'Make it cool,' until we saw the shadow of the hillocks. Then the Prophet said, 'Indeed the intensity of heat is from the blast of Hell; so when the heat is intense, delay the prayer due to coolness.' [Bukhari, Bab al-Ibrad bil-Zuhr fi al-Safar, p. 91, no. 539; Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt Salat al-Zuhr, p. 70, no. 402] A hillock is low; its shadow appears below only when every thing's shadow has exceeded one time. This indicates that Zuhr was offered after one shadow. Therefore the time of Zuhr extends to two shadows. (2) From Abdullah ibn Umar that they narrated from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'When the heat is intense, delay the prayer due to coolness; indeed the intensity of heat is from the blast of Hell.' [Bukhari, Bab al-Ibrad bil-Zuhr fi Shiddat al-Harr, p. 90, no. 533; Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt Salat al-Zuhr, p. 70, no. 402] This hadith also indicates delaying Zuhr in heat, suggesting that Zuhr was prayed at two shadows because in Arabia the heat lasts until two shadows. (3) As for both of them, the time of Zuhr begins from zawal. The proof is this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah came out when the sun declined and prayed Zuhr. [Bukhari, Bab Waqt al-Zuhr 'ind al-Zawal, p. 91, no. 54] From this hadith it is known that as soon as the sun declines, the time of Zuhr begins. The proof of the Sahibayn is the hadith of the imamate of Jibril. Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet said: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice. He prayed Zuhr the first time when the shadow was like a sandal strap, then he prayed Asr when everything's shadow was like...
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of Zuhr time and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author starts with the ruling: Zuhr time is from zawal (sun's decline) until the shadow of an object becomes either twice its height (according to Abu Hanifa) or once its height (according to the Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). This excludes the shadow at midday (zawal time). The author notes that Imam Tahawi adopted the Sahibayn's view. Then, evidence is presented: (1) Abu Hanifa's proof: The hadith of Abu Dhar where the Prophet delayed Zuhr until the shadow of hillocks appeared. Ibn Qutaybah's interpretation: a hillock's shadow becomes visible only when the sun has declined significantly, indicating the time extended beyond one shadow. (2) A similar hadith from Ibn Umar. (3) Both agree that Zuhr begins at zawal (proof from Anas). The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith of Jibril's imamate, where Jibril prayed Zuhr at the beginning of its time (shadow like a sandal strap) on the first day and at the end of its time (shadow like a person's height) on the second day. The text ends mid-sentence. The Hanafi mu'tamad (relied-upon position) according to classical Hanafi texts is usually Abu Hanifa's view (two shadows), but there is a strong minority position from the Sahibayn adopted by Tahawi.

Key Terms
زوال شمس (zawal al-shams): The moment when the sun passes the meridian and begins to decline; start of Zuhr time.
مثل (mithl): The length of a shadow relative to the object's height; e.g., one mithl means shadow equals object height.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the end time of Zuhr prayer?
A) Until the shadow becomes like a sandal strap.
B) Until the shadow becomes equal to the object's height.
C) Until the shadow becomes twice the object's height (excluding midday shadow).
D) Until sunset.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains an internal ikhtilaf on Zuhr end time; the mufta bihi is generally Abu Hanifa's two-shadow view, but Tahawi followed the Sahibayn.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Zuhr Time End: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains the Zuhr time dispute with proofs from hadith and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Zuhr ends at one shadow (Sahibayn) or two shadows (Abu Hanifa); the relied-upon view is one shadow.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about when the time for Zuhr prayer ends. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students disagreed on whether it ends when a shadow equals the object's height or when it doubles. Their proofs come from different hadiths, and later scholars like Imam Tahawi resolved the difference. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate evidence within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
What does each imam say exactly? Abu Hanifa: Zuhr until mithlayn (two shadows). Sahibayn: until mithl (one shadow).
Both exclude the midday shadow (zill al-istawa).
2
Identify the shared starting point
Both agree Zuhr begins at zawal (decline) and that the midday shadow is not counted.
The dispute is only about the end point.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Which hadith does he cite? The hadith of Abu Dharr about delaying until shadows of hills appear, implying more than one shadow.
Also the hadith about delaying in heat.
4
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The hadith of Jibril, where Jibril prayed Zuhr when shadow was like a shoestring and later when it was like the object's height, indicating the end at one shadow.
This hadith is more explicit.
5
Determine the preferred view
Imam Tahawi and later Hanafi authorities favored the Sahibayn's view; it is the mufta bihi.
Most Hanafi prayer timetables follow one shadow.

الاستواء . واختار الثانى الطحاوى وهو قول الصاحبين . (۲۹۸) وقت العصر من ابتداء الزيادة على
ظله
. وصلى المرة الثانية الظهر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثله لوقت العصر بالامس ..... ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين . ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء مواقيت الصلوة عن النبي الله ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب المواقیت، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ظہر کا وقت
مثل اول پر ختم ہو گیا، اور عصر کا وقت مثل اول پر شروع ہو گیا، اس لئے مثل اول کے ختم ہونے تک ظہر کا وقت رہتا ہے۔ لغت : زوال الشمس : سور نکلنے اور سورج ڈوبنے کے درمیان کو آدھا دن [ نصف النہار ] کہتے ہیں ، اس سے ذرا سا سورج ڈھل جائے اس کو زوال الشمس، کہتے ہیں۔ خل الاستواء: نصف النہار کے وقت جو سایہ ہوتا ہے اس کو ظل الاستواء، کہتے ہیں ، اسی کو د سایہ اصلی بھی کہتے ہیں۔ مثل اول : مثلا آدمی ساڑھے پانچ فٹ کا ہے تو زمین پر اس کا سایہ ساڑھے پانچ فٹ لمبا ہو جائے، یہ آدمی کا ایک مثل سایہ ہوا، سایہ اصلی کے علاوہ ایک مثل سایہ ہو جائے تو یہ شل اول ، ہوا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک یہاں ظہر کا وقت ختم ہو جائے گا اور عصر کا وقت شروع ہو جائے گا۔ مثلیہ : دوشل ، آدمی ساڑھے پانچ فٹ کا ہے، اور زمین پر اس کا سایہ!! [ گیارہ] فٹ لمبا پڑنے لگ گیا تو یہ دومثل ، ہو گیا ، سایہ اصلی کے علاوہ اس دوشل پر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ظہر کا وقت ختم ہوتا ہے ۔ اور اس کے بعد عصر کا
وقت شروع ہوتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۹۸) [۳] عصر کا وقت ایک مثل سے یاد و شل سے زیادہ ہونے سے غروب آفتاب تک ہے ۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دوشل کے بعد سے عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا ، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک مثل کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا ، اور آفتاب ڈوبنے سے پہلے تک رہے گا۔
وجه: (1) وسبح بحمد ربك قبل طلوع الشمس وقبل غروبها ( آیت ۱۳۰، سوره طه ۲۰) غروب سے پہلے نماز پڑھنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز عصر کا وقت سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے تک ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الله الله قال من ادرك من الصبح ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرک الصبح و من ادرک ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس فقد ادرک العصر ) بخاری شریف، باب من ادرک من الفجر ركعتة ، ص ۹۷، نمبر ۷۹ ۵/ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فیمن ادرک رکعته من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس ، ص ۵۲ نمبر ۱۸۶) سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے عصر کی ایک رکعت پالے تو گویا کہ پوری عصر کی نماز پالی۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غروب آفتاب سے پہلے تک عصر کا وقت ہے (۳) آفتاب زرد ہونے کے بعد نماز عصر ہو جائے گی البتہ مکروہ ہوگی ، اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ قال : دخلنا على انس بن مالک بعد الظهر فقام يصلى العصر .... تلك صلوة المنافقين ، يجلس أحدهم حتى اذا اصفرت الشمس
Times of prayer. (297) The time of Zuhr is from the sun's decline until the shadow of everything becomes two times its height or one time its height, aside from the shadow at midday. Rather, the spreading light on the horizon is the true dawn. (2) In the verse there is also indication: 'And eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread of dawn' (Quran 2:187). By 'becoming distinct' is meant the clear appearance of dawn which occurs at the time of true dawn. Translation (297) [2] The time of Zuhr is from the sun's decline until the shadow of everything becomes two shadows or one shadow, aside from the shadow at the time of equinox. And the other saying (that Zuhr time lasts until one shadow) was chosen by Imam Tahawi; this is the saying of the Sahibayn. Elaboration: The sun reaches the meridian and then declines slightly – this is called the sun's decline (zawal al-shams). From there Zuhr time begins. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it remains until two shadows; according to the Sahibayn, until one shadow. After that, Asr time begins. Imam Tahawi chose this. Proof: (1) The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is this hadith: From Abu Dharr: We were with the Messenger of Allah (SAW) on a journey. The caller wanted to call the adhan for Zuhr, but the Prophet (SAW) said 'Wait for it to cool', then he wanted to call, and he said 'Wait for it to cool' until we saw the shadows of the hills. Then the Prophet (SAW) said: 'The intensity of heat is from the raging of Hell, so when it is hot, delay the prayer.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Ibrad bi al-Zuhr fi al-Safar, p.91, no.539; Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt Salat al-Zuhr, p.70, no.40). A small hill – its shadow appears below – this can only happen when everyone's shadow is more than one shadow. From this it is understood that Zuhr prayer was performed after one shadow. Therefore, Zuhr time is until two shadows. (2) From Abdullah ibn Umar that they narrated from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) that he said: 'When it is hot, delay the prayer, for intensity of heat is from the raging of Hell.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Ibrad bi al-Zuhr fi Shiddat al-Harr, p.90, no.533; Abu Dawud, Bab Waqt Salat al-Zuhr, p.70, no.402). In this hadith also, delay of Zuhr in heat is mentioned, indicating that Zuhr prayer would have been performed at two shadows, because in Arabia the heat remains until two shadows. (3) As for both, the time of Zuhr begins from the decline, and its proof is this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) went out when the sun declined and prayed Zuhr. (Bukhari, Bab Waqt al-Zuhr 'ind al-Zawal, p.99, no.54). From this hadith it is known that Zuhr time begins as soon as the sun declines. The proof of the Sahibayn is the hadith of Jibril's imamate: Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Jibril led me in prayer at the House twice. He prayed Zuhr the first time when the shadow was like a shoestring, then he prayed Asr when everything's shadow was like its height.' And he chose the second (view) of Tahawi, which is the saying of the Sahibayn. (298) The time of Asr is from the beginning of the increase beyond its shadow. And he prayed the second time Zuhr when the shadow of everything was like its height (for the Asr time of the previous day) ... then he turned to Jibril and said: 'O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Mawaqit al-Salat 'an al-Nabi, p.42, no.149; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Mawaqit, p.68, no.393). In this hadith, Zuhr time ended at the first shadow, and Asr time began at the first shadow, so Zuhr time remains until the end of the first shadow. Lexicon: Zawal al-shams: the halfway point between sunrise and sunset [noon], when the sun declines slightly – this is called zawal al-shams. Zill al-istawa: the shadow that occurs at noon – called the original shadow (saya asli). First shadow (mithl awwal): e.g. a person is 5.5 feet tall, his shadow on the ground becomes 5.5 feet long – this is one like (mithl) of the person, aside from the original shadow, so it is the first shadow. According to the Sahibayn, here Zuhr time ends and Asr time begins. Two shadows (mithlayn): a person is 5.5 feet tall, and his shadow on the ground becomes 11 feet long – this is two like (mithlayn), aside from the original shadow. At this two-like, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Zuhr time ends, and after that Asr time begins. Translation (298) [3] The time of Asr is from when (the shadow) exceeds one like or two likes until sunset. Elaboration: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Asr time begins after two likes; according to the Sahibayn, Asr time begins after one like, and it remains until before sunset. Proof: (1) 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before sunrise and before sunset' (Quran 20:130). Praying before sunset means that the time of Asr prayer is until before sunset. (2) In a hadith: From Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.' (Bukhari, Bab man Adraka min al-Fajr rak'atan, p.97, no.795; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi man Adraka rak'ah min al-Asr qabl an taghruba al-shams, p.52, no.186). If he catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset, it is as if he caught the entire Asr prayer. This means that the time of Asr is until before sunset. (3) After the sun turns yellow, Asr prayer is valid but makruh. Its proof is this hadith: He said: We entered upon Anas ibn Malik after Zuhr, and he stood to pray Asr ... 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites: one of them sits until when the sun becomes yellow ...'
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer and the beginning of Asr prayer. The author explains the two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Zuhr time extends until the shadow of everything becomes twice its height (mithlayn) besides the midday shadow (zill al-istawa), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that Zuhr time ends when the shadow becomes equal to the object's height (mithl) besides the midday shadow. The author notes that Imam Tahawi chose the Sahibayn's view. The proof for Abu Hanifa is based on a hadith where the Prophet delayed Zuhr until the shadows of hills appeared, indicating a shadow longer than one mithl, implying that the Prophet prayed after one mithl, so Zuhr time extends to two mithl. Also, the hadith about delaying in heat suggests praying at two mithl because heat remains that long. The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Jibril, where Jibril led the Prophet in prayer at the House twice; the first time he prayed Zuhr when the shadow was like a shoestring (very short), and the second day he prayed Zuhr when the shadow was like the object's height. The Prophet said the time is between these two times, implying Zuhr ends at one mithl. The author then defines key terms: zawal al-shams (declining from noon), zill al-istawa (midday shadow), mithl awwal (one like), mithlayn (two likes). The passage also discusses Asr time, which begins according to the respective views: after two mithl for Abu Hanifa, after one mithl for the Sahibayn, and both agree it ends at sunset. Proofs for Asr time include Quranic verse 20:130 and hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset. A hadith warns against praying when the sun turns yellow, which is makruh tanzihan. This passage is typical of a commentary (sharh) that expands on the matn by providing proofs and resolving differences.

Key Terms
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The sun's decline from the meridian; the start of Zuhr time.
ظل الاستواء (zill al-istawa): The shadow cast at noon when the sun is at its zenith; this shadow is not counted in measuring the prayer times.
مثل (mithl): The shadow equal in length to the object's height, excluding the midday shadow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does the time of Zuhr prayer end?
A) When the shadow becomes equal to the object's height (one mithl)
B) When the shadow becomes twice the object's height (two mithl)
C) At sunset
D) At the beginning of the decline

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on Zuhr's end: Abu Hanifa (two shadows) vs. the Sahibayn (one shadow); the relied-upon view is one shadow, as chosen by Imam Tahawi.

Salah — Prayer

Time of Asr Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shadow Length
States the Hanafi ruling for Asr time with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the beginning of Asr time, identify the mufta bihi, and apply the ruling to determine the valid prayer window.

Core Idea
Asr begins when the shadow exceeds one length (mufta bihi) or two lengths (Abu Hanifa); both are based on hadith.

The time of Asr is a critical condition for the validity of the prayer. Within the Hanafi school, there is a known dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, over exactly when Asr time begins. This lesson unpacks that dispute, explores the evidence, and settles on the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the dispute
Recognize that the passage discusses the beginning of Asr time. The dispute is about the exact shadow length after which Asr starts.
The end time (sunset) is agreed upon.
2
State each position with precision
Imam Abu Hanifa: Asr begins when the shadow of an object is twice its height (excluding the noon shadow). The Sahibayn: Asr begins when the shadow is once its height.
Use the terms مثل اول and دومثل correctly.
3
Examine the proofs
The hadith of Jibril shows the Prophet praying Asr on two consecutive days: once at one shadow and once at two shadows. Other hadiths confirm the end time at sunset and the disliked time after yellowing.
The proofs are all hadith ahad, which is why ikhtilaf is possible.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
Al-Tahawi chose the Sahibayn view based on the practice of the Prophet and ease. This is now the mufta bihi (operative view) in the school.
The tarjih authority is Fat-h al-Qadir and the later Hanafi masters.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a Hanafi should begin Asr when the shadow is one length after noon. Delaying until two shadows is permissible but not the preferred time.
The practical difference (thamarah) is the actual start time for prayer.

Source Text

[ گیارہ] فٹ لمبا پڑنے لگ گیا تو یہ دومثل ، ہو گیا ، سایہ اصلی کے علاوہ اس دوشل پر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ظہر کا وقت ختم ہوتا ہے ۔ اور اس کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۲۹۸) [۳] عصر کا وقت ایک مثل سے یاد و شل سے زیادہ ہونے سے غروب آفتاب تک ہے ۔ تشریح : امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دوشل کے بعد سے عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا ، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک مثل کے بعد عصر کا وقت شروع ہوگا ، اور آفتاب ڈوبنے سے پہلے تک رہے گا۔
وجه: (1) وسبح بحمد ربك قبل طلوع الشمس وقبل غروبها ( آیت ۱۳۰، سوره طه ۲۰) غروب سے پہلے نماز پڑھنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نماز عصر کا وقت سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے تک ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان رسول الله الله الله قال من ادرك من الصبح ركعة قبل ان تطلع الشمس فقد ادرک الصبح و من ادرک ركعة من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس فقد ادرک العصر ) بخاری شریف، باب من ادرک من الفجر ركعتة ، ص ۹۷، نمبر ۷۹ ۵/ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فیمن ادرک ركعته من العصر قبل ان تغرب الشمس ، ص ۵۲ نمبر ۱۸۶) سورج غروب ہونے سے پہلے عصر کی ایک رکعت پالے تو گویا کہ پوری عصر کی نماز پالی۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غروب آفتاب سے پہلے تک عصر کا وقت ہے (۳) آفتاب زرد ہونے کے بعد نماز عصر ہو جائے گی البتہ مکروہ ہوگی ، اسکی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ قال : دخلنا على انس بن مالک بعد الظهر فقام يصلى العصر .... تلك صلوة المنافقين ، يجلس أحدهم حتى اذا اصفرت الشمس فكانت بين قرني شيطان أو على قرني الشيطان ، قام فنقر أربعا لا يذكر الله عز وجل فيها الا قليلا ً ۔(ابو داود شریف ، باب وقت العصر ، ص ،اے، نمبر (۴۱۳) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ نماز ہو جائے گی مگر مگر وہ ہوگی (۴) ۔ دوسری حدیث بھی ہے عن عبد الله بن عمران النبي عل الله قال اذا صليتم الفجر ... فاذا صليتم العصر فانه وقت الى أن تصـفر الشمس ( مسلم شریف، باب اوقات الصلوات النمس ،ص ۲۴۷ نمبر ۱۳۸۵/۶۱۲ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی مواقیت الصلواۃ ، ص ۴۲، نمبر (۱۵) اس حدیث میں سورج زرد ہونے تک مستحب وقت بتایا ہے۔
Times of prayer. The second opinion was chosen by al-Tahawi, and it is the saying of the two companions. (298) The time of Asr is from the beginning of the increase over its shadow. And he prayed the second Zuhr when the shadow of everything was like it, for the time of Asr yesterday... then he turned to Jibril and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) In this hadith, the time of Zuhr ends at one shadow, and the time of Asr begins at one shadow, so the time of Zuhr remains until the end of one shadow. Lexicon: Zawal al-shams: the midpoint between sunrise and sunset, when the sun has slightly declined. Zill al-istawa: the shadow at midday, also called the original shadow. First shadow: e.g., a person 5.5 feet tall, his shadow on the ground becomes 5.5 feet long; that is one shadow of the person. When there is one shadow beyond the original shadow, that is the first shadow. According to the two companions, here the time of Zuhr ends and the time of Asr begins. Second shadow: 5.5 feet tall, his shadow on the ground becomes eleven feet long; that is two shadows. When there are two shadows beyond the original shadow, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the time of Zuhr ends and after that the time of Asr begins. Translation: (298) [3] The time of Asr is from the excess of one or two shadows until sunset. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the time of Asr begins after two shadows, and according to the two companions, it begins after one shadow, and it remains until before sunset. Proof: (1) 'And glorify the praises of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting' (Surah Taha, 20:130) – praying before sunset means that the time of Asr is until sunset. (2) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.' (Bukhari, Tirmidhi) So the time of Asr is until sunset. (3) The Asr prayer after the sun turns yellow is valid but makruh. The proof is the hadith: 'We entered upon Anas ibn Malik after Zuhr, and he stood to pray Asr... That is the prayer of the hypocrites: one sits until the sun turns yellow and is between the two horns of Satan, then he stands and pecks four (rak'ahs), remembering Allah only a little.' (Abu Dawud) This indicates that the prayer is valid but makruh. (4) Another hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When you pray Fajr... and when you pray Asr, its time is until the sun turns yellow.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) This indicates the preferred time until yellowing.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the beginning time of Asr prayer. The author first presents the ruling text (matn) stating that Asr time starts from the increase beyond one or two shadows until sunset. He then explains the lexical terms: 'zawal al-shams' is the slight decline of the sun from the meridian, and 'zill al-istawa' is the noontime shadow. The 'first shadow' is when the shadow of an object equals its height, excluding the noontime shadow. The 'second shadow' is when it is twice the height. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), Asr begins after the first shadow, i.e., when the shadow exceeds one times the height beyond the original shadow. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it begins after the second shadow, i.e., when it exceeds two times the height. The author then provides proofs from the Quran and Hadith, all indicating that Asr time ends at sunset, and that praying when the sun is yellow is valid but disliked.

Key Terms
ظل الاستواء (zill al-istawa): The shadow at noon when the sun is at its zenith; the shortest shadow of the day.
مثل اول (mithl awwal): When the shadow of an object equals its height, excluding the original noon shadow.
دومثل (mithlayn): When the shadow of an object is twice its height, excluding the original noon shadow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately after the sun begins to decline (zawal).
B) When the shadow of an object equals its height, excluding the noon shadow.
C) When the shadow of an object is twice its height, excluding the noon shadow.
D) When the sun turns yellow.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that Asr time begins when the shadow of an object equals its height, excluding the noon shadow.

Time of Maghrib Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shafaq
States the Hanafi ruling for Maghrib time with intra-madhhab dispute on shafaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling for the end time of Maghrib and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the definition of shafaq.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends at the disappearance of the red glow (shafaq ahmar) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

The time for Maghrib prayer is between sunset and the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq). However, the exact meaning of shafaq is disputed within the Hanafi school. This lesson explains the two positions and why the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Maghrib prayer is wajib with a specific time window: from sunset until the disappearance of the shafaq.
2
State the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn: Maghrib ends at the disappearance of the red glow (shafaq ahmar).
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that Maghrib ends at the disappearance of the white glow (shafaq abyad).
4
Examine the proofs for each position
Sahibayn rely on hadith that Maghrib time ends when the shafaq disappears, understanding shafaq as the red glow. Abu Hanifa uses analogy with Fajr (white spreading light) and a hadith about the Prophet praying Isha when the horizon becomes dark.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Following Sahibayn, Maghrib must be prayed before the red glow disappears (approx. 1.5 hours after sunset). Following Abu Hanifa, it can be delayed until the white glow disappears (approx. 30 minutes later).
The mufta bihi view is more cautious and easier to observe in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثل او المثلين الى غروب الشمس . (۲۹۹) والمغرب منه الى غروب الشفق الاحمر على المفتى
، فكانت بين قرني شيطان أو على قرني الشيطان ، قام فنقر أربعا لا يذكر الله عز وجل فيها الا قليلا ً ۔(ابو داود شریف ، باب وقت العصر ، ص ،اے، نمبر (۴۱۳) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ نماز ہو جائے گی مگر مگر وہ ہوگی (۴) ۔ دوسری حدیث بھی ہے عن عبد الله بن عمران النبي عل الله قال اذا صليتم الفجر ... فاذا صليتم العصر فانه وقت الى أن تصـفر الشمس ( مسلم شریف، باب اوقات الصلوات النمس ،ص ۲۴۷ نمبر ۱۳۸۵/۶۱۲ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی مواقیت الصلواۃ ، ص ۴۲، نمبر (۱۵) اس حدیث میں سورج زرد ہونے تک مستحب وقت بتایا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۲۹۹) [۴] مغرب کا وقت غروب سے لے کر شفق احمر کے غروب تک ہے ۔ مفتی بہ قول پر ۔ تشریح : سورج غروب ہونے کے بعد سے مغرب کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک شفق احمر کے غروب تک رہتا ہے ہمفتی بہ قول یہی ہے ۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شفق احمد کے بعد شفق ابیض آتا ہے وہاں تک مغرب کا وقت رہتا ہے۔ البتہ حضرت جبرئیل نے دونوں دن ایک ہی وقت میں مغرب کی نماز پڑھائی ہے اس لئے اول وقت میں پڑھنا سنت ہے۔ وجه : اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمران النبي عل الله قال اذا صليتم الفجر ... فاذا صليتم المغرب فانه وقت الى ان يسقط الشفق . ( مسلم شریف ، باب اوقات الصلوات احمس ،ص ۲۴۷ نمبر ۱۳۸۵/۶۱۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی مواقیت الصلواۃ ، ص ۴۲، نمبر (۱۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کا وقت شفق کے غروب ہونے تک رہتا ہے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة قال : قال رسول الله الله الله ان للصلاة أولا و آخراً .... و ان اول وقت المغرب حين تغرب الشمس و ان آخر وقتها حين يغيب الشفق - ( ترمذی شریف، باب منه ( یعنی ما جاء فی مواقیت الصلوة ) ص ۲۲ نمبر ۱۵ مسلم شریف ، باب اوقات الصلوة النمس جس ۲۴۷ نمبر ۱۳۸۹/۶۱۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مغرب کا وقت شفق غائب ہونے تک ہے۔ اب کون سا شفق مراد ہے اس کی تفصیل نیچے ہے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل : (۱) فجر میں بیاض مستطیر فجر کا وقت ہے۔ اسی طرح بیاض مستطیر مغرب کا وقت ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ دونوں ایک ہی طرح ہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت ابا مسعود الانصارى يقول ... ويصلي المغرب حين تسقط الشمس ويصلى العشاء حين يسود الافق وربما اخرها حتى يجتمع الناس ۔ ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المواقیت، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ عشا کی نماز افق کالا ہونے کے بعد پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اورمکمل کالاشفق ابیض ڈوبنے کے بعد ہو گا اس لئے مغرب کا وقت شفق ابیض تک ہوا۔ (۳) اس کی تائید اس اثر سے ہوتی ہے۔ کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز ان صلوا صلوة العشاء اذا ذهب بياض الافق فيما بينكم و بين ثلث الليل (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب
One or two shadows until sunset. (299) And Maghrib is from it (sunset) to the disappearance of the red glow, according to the relied-upon view... it was between the two horns of Satan or on the two horns of Satan, he stood and pecked four (rak'ahs), mentioning Allah only a little. (Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that the prayer is valid but makruh. (4) Another hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When you pray Fajr... and when you pray Asr, its time is until the sun turns yellow.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates the preferred time until yellowing. Translation: (299) [4] Maghrib time is from sunset to the disappearance of the red glow, according to the mufta bihi view. Explanation: Maghrib time begins after sunset, and according to the two companions, it lasts until the red glow disappears – this is the mufta bihi view. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the red glow comes the white glow, and Maghrib time lasts until that. However, Jibril prayed Maghrib at the same time on both days, so it is sunnah to pray at the beginning. Proof: This is evidenced by the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When you pray Fajr... and when you pray Maghrib, its time is until the shafaq disappears.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) This shows that Maghrib time remains until the shafaq disappears. (2) From Abu Hurairah: 'Indeed prayer has a first and last time... the first time of Maghrib is when the sun sets, and its last time is when the shafaq disappears.' (Tirmidhi, Muslim) This hadith states that Maghrib time is until the shafaq disappears. Now which shafaq is meant? The detail is below. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: (1) In Fajr, the white spreading light is the time of Fajr. Similarly, the white spreading light should be the time of Maghrib because both are similar. (2) Hadith: 'I heard Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari say... he prayed Maghrib when the sun set, and prayed Isha when the horizon became dark, and sometimes delayed it until people gathered.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith states that the Prophet prayed Isha after the horizon became dark, and complete darkness is after the white glow disappears, so Maghrib time is until the white glow. (3) This is supported by the athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'He wrote: Pray the Isha prayer when the whiteness of the horizon disappears, between that and one third of the night.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time of Maghrib prayer. The author presents the ruling: Maghrib time lasts from sunset until the disappearance of the red glow (shafaq ahmar). This is the mufta bihi (relied upon) view, which is that of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it lasts until the disappearance of the white glow (shafaq abyad). The author brings proofs for the Sahibayn view: hadith stating that Maghrib time ends when the shafaq disappears, and that the Prophet would pray Isha when the horizon became dark. For Abu Hanifa: analogy with Fajr (white spreading light) and the hadith about Isha being delayed until the horizon darkens, implying Maghrib time continues until then. The preferred view is the Sahibayn view because it is more cautious and supported by most hadith.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; can be red (ahmar) or white (abyad).
الشفق الاحمر (al-shafaq al-ahmar): The red twilight that appears immediately after sunset.
الشفق الابيض (al-shafaq al-abyad): The white twilight that appears after the red has faded, leading to complete darkness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, when does the time of Maghrib end?
A) Immediately after sunset.
B) When the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) disappears.
C) When the white twilight (shafaq abyad) disappears.
D) When the horizon becomes completely dark.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib prayer time ends at the disappearance of the red glow according to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, though Imam Abu Hanifa held it ends at the white glow.

Salah — Prayer

End Time of Maghrib: The Shafaq Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the end time of Maghrib prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the end time of Maghrib, identify the mufta bihi, and apply the ruling to determine whether a Maghrib prayer is ada or qada.

Core Idea
Maghrib time ends when the red twilight disappears – that is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute about the end time of Maghrib prayer. The core question is whether the twilight (shafaq) that marks the end is red or white. Although Imam Abu Hanifa held that Maghrib continues until the white twilight fades, the Sahibayn and later authorities adopted the red twilight view, which is now the mufta bihi. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate proofs and recognize the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed point
Locate the exact issue: What color twilight ends Maghrib time? Abu Hanifa says white, Sahibayn say red.
The term 'shafaq' is ambiguous and each side interprets it differently.
2
State the mufta bihi position
The text explicitly says 'ala al-mufta' (upon the relied-upon). That is the Sahibayn's view: end of red twilight.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa and practice.
3
Examine the proofs for each side
List the dalil: For Sahibayn – hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar and Abu Huraira. For Abu Hanifa – qiyas with Fajr, hadith of Abu Mas'ud, and athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
Pay attention to how each side uses the same texts differently.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If someone prays after red but before white: according to Abu Hanifa it is ada; according to Sahibayn it is qada. The mufta bihi makes it qada.
This directly affects whether the prayer is valid in time or must be repeated.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific time, decide if Maghrib is still valid based on the mufta bihi.
Use the criterion: red twilight must still be visible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح: سورج غروب ہونے کے بعد سے مغرب کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک شفق احمر کے غروب تک رہتا ہے۔ مفتی بہ قول یہی ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شفق احمر کے بعد شفق ابیض آتا ہے وہاں تک مغرب کا وقت رہتا ہے۔ البتہ حضرت جبرئیل نے دونوں دن ایک ہی وقت میں مغرب کی نماز پڑھائی ہے اس لئے اول وقت میں پڑھنا سنت ہے۔
وجه: اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: عن عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله عنهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: إذا صليتم المغرب فإنه وقت إلى أن يسقط الشفق. (مسلم، ترمذی)

(ابو داود) (3) اثر: كتب عمر بن عبد العزيز: أن صلوا صلاة العشاء إذا ذهب بياض الأفق. (مصنف عبد الرزاق)
(299) [4] And Maghrib is from it (i.e., from sunset) until the disappearance of the red twilight, according to the relied-upon view. Explanation: The time of Maghrib begins after sunset, and according to the Sahibayn, it remains until the disappearance of the red twilight. This is the mufta bihi view. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the red twilight comes the white twilight, and the time remains until then. However, Jibril (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at the same time on both days, so praying at the beginning time is sunnah. Proof: The evidence is this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'When you pray Maghrib, its time is until the twilight disappears.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) And from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed for prayer there is a beginning and an end... and indeed the last time of Maghrib is when the twilight disappears.' (Tirmidhi, Muslim) Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: (1) In Fajr, the spreading whiteness is the time of Fajr; similarly, the spreading whiteness should be the time of Maghrib, because both are alike. (2) Hadith: I heard Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari saying: 'He prays Maghrib when the sun sets, and prays Isha when the horizon becomes dark.' (Abu Dawud) (3) Effect: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote: 'Pray Isha when the whiteness of the horizon disappears.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq)
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end time of Maghrib prayer. The matn states that according to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, Maghrib time extends from sunset until the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) disappears. The commentator explains that this is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the time continues until the white twilight (shafaq abyad) also disappears. Despite this difference, the sunnah is to pray at the earliest time, as Jibril (AS) led the Prophet (SAW) in Maghrib at the same time on the first and second day. The text then provides proofs: For the Sahibayn, hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar and Abu Huraira state that Maghrib time lasts until the twilight (shafaq) disappears; the word 'shafaq' is commonly understood as red. For Abu Hanifa, three proofs are given: (1) Qiyas: Just as the spreading whiteness (bayad mustatir) in Fajr indicates the time, similarly the whiteness after sunset should indicate Maghrib time, since both are analogous. (2) A hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari reporting that the Prophet (SAW) would pray Isha only when the horizon became completely dark, implying Maghrib is before that, i.e., while there is still whiteness. (3) The practice of Caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz instructing to pray Isha when the whiteness of the horizon fades, again indicating that Maghrib time includes the period when whiteness remains. The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn, meaning that in practice, one must pray Maghrib before the red twilight ends.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; the reddish or whitish glow in the sky.
الشفق الأحمر (al-shafaq al-ahmar): The red twilight that appears after sunset and fades into darkness.
الشفق الأبيض (al-shafaq al-abyad): The white twilight that remains after the red twilight has faded, before complete darkness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, when does the time for Maghrib prayer end?
A) At sunset
B) With the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq ahmar)
C) With the disappearance of the white twilight (shafaq abyad)
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that Maghrib time ends with the disappearance of the red twilight; praying after that but before white twilight renders the prayer qada.

The Definition of Shafaq and Its Effect on Isha Prayer Time
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shafaq definition and its effect on Isha start time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute over the definition of shafaq, explain the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi ruling for when Isha begins.

Core Idea
The start of Isha prayer depends on whether shafaq is defined as red or white twilight; the Hanafi school follows the Sahibayn's view that it is the redness.

Determining the correct time for Isha prayer is essential for valid salah. However, within the Hanafi school, there is a classical dispute over what precisely constitutes the 'shafaq' (twilight) whose disappearance marks the end of Maghrib and the beginning of Isha. This lesson unpacks the two positions, their proofs, and the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue and its stake
The issue is not the obligation of Isha (which is wajib) but the moment when its time begins. This affects the end of Maghrib time as well. Two definitions of shafaq are at play: red twilight (shafaq ahmar) and white twilight (shafaq abyad).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
According to Abu Hanifa, shafaq is the white twilight (bayad mustatil), so Maghrib time extends until the white disappears and Isha begins then. His proof includes the Quranic phrase 'ghasaq al-layl' (darkness of the night), implying complete darkness after white twilight.
Also relies on the spread-out whiteness (bayad mustatir) still being part of Maghrib.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, shafaq is the red twilight (shafaq ahmar). Their proof is the hadith 'al-shafaq al-humrah' (the twilight is the redness) and the Jibril hadith where the Prophet prayed Isha when the twilight disappeared (interpreted as redness).
The majority of scholars (jumhur) including Shafi'i and Malik side with the Sahibayn.
4
Identify the mufta bihi ruling and the thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn: shafaq is the redness, so Isha begins after the red twilight vanishes. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's view, Maghrib extends longer and Isha starts later; under the mufta bihi, Isha starts earlier.
This difference matters especially in summer or at higher latitudes where twilight durations vary.
5
Confirm the end time of Isha
Regardless of the dispute over its start, all agree that Isha time ends at dawn (subh sadiq). The passage provides proofs from hadith and companion statements establishing this.
Thus the disagreement is only over the beginning, not the ending.

وقت العشاء الاخرة ، ج اول ص ۱۴۱۰، نمبر ۲۱۱۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ افق کے بیاض جانے یعنی شفق ابیض کے ڈوبنے کے بعد نماز عشاء کا وقت ہوتا ہے۔ (۴) اس آیت کے کنایہ سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اقم الصلوة لدلوك الشمس الى غسق الليل و قرآن الفجر ۔ ( آیت ۷۸، سورۃ الاسراء (۱۷) اس آیت میں غسق اللیل ہے، کہ اندھیرا ہو جائے تو عشاء کی نماز پڑھو جس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ شفق ابیض ڈوبنے کے بعد عشاء کا وقت ہے کیونکہ پورا کالا اسی وقت ہوتا ہے ۔ اور اس سے پہلے تک مغرب کا وقت ہے۔

( دارقطنی ، باب في صفة المغرب واصح ، ج اول ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۰۴ ارسن للبیھقی ، باب دخول وقت العشاء بغيد به الشفق ، ج اول ص ۵۴۸ نمبر ۱۷۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سرخ شفق تک مغرب کا وقت ہے ۔(۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عـمـر قـال : الشفق الحمرة - ( دار قطنی ، باب في صفته المغرب واصبح ، ج اول ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۰۴۵رسن للبیھقی ، باب دخول وقت العشاء بغیو به الشفق ، ج اول ص ۵۴۸ نمبر ۱۷۴۲) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ شفق وہ سرخی ہے۔
شفق احمر او شفق ابیض کیا ہے
شفق احمر ، اور شفق ابیض : آفتاب ڈوبنے کے بعد پہلے سرخی آتی ہے پھر سفید روشنی پھیلی ہوئی ہوتی ہے اس کو، بیاض مستطیر ، کہتے ہیں کیونکہ یہ روشنی پھیلی ہوئی ہے اس کے بعد یہی سفید روشنی لمبی ہو جاتی ہے جس کو بیاض مستطیل، کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ لبی روشنی ہے ،اس کے بعد افق پر مکمل اندھیرا چھا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک سرخی کے بعد جو بیاض مستطیر ہے [ پھیلی ہوئی سفید روشنی ] وہاں تک مغرب کا وقت ہے۔ اس کے بعد عشا کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے شفق کیسے ھوتا ھے : افق کے قریب بھاپ اور نمی بہت ہوتی ہے، سورج جب ڈوب جاتا ہے تو اسکی روشنی بھاپ اور نمی سے گزر کر ہماری طرف آنے لگتی ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ بھاپ کے درمیان سے گزر کر روشنی آئے تو وہ لال نظر آتی ہے اور تھوڑی پھیلی ہو کی نظر آتی ہے ، اسی لئے سورج ڈوبنے کے بعد جو روشنی نظر آتی ہے وہ لال ہوتی ہے جسکو شفق احمر کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن سورج جب بارہ ڈگری نیچے چلا جاتا ہے تو افق کے پاس جو بھاپ اور نمی ہے اس سے گزر کر روشنی نہیں آتی بلکہ سورج کی روشنی آسمان کی طرف لمبی ہوتی ہوئی نظر آتی ہے ، چونکہ وہ بھاپ اور نمی سے گزر کر نہیں آتی اسلئے وہ روشنی سفید نظر آتی ہے ، اور بہت ہلکی ہوتی ہے شفق احمر کے بعد
مسلسل دیکھتے رہیں تب اس کا پتہ چلے گا ورنہ جلدی پتہ نہیں چلتا۔ اس کو شفق ابیض کہتے ہیں۔ ناچیز نے اس کا تجربہ کئی بار اپنے ملک جھار کھنڈ میں کیا ہے۔ ( شارح ماہر فلکیات ہیں )
ترجمه : ( ۳۰۰) [۵] عشاء اور وتر کا وقت وہاں سے صبح صادق تک ہے۔
تشریح : صاحبین کے قول پر شفق احمد کے بعد ، اور امام اعظم کے قول پر شفق ابیض کے بعد عشاء کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے اور صبح صادق تک رہتا ہے وجه : (۱) عشاء کے اول وقت کے سلسلے میں کئی حدیثیں گزرگئیں ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال امني جبرئيل عند البيت مرتين .... ثم صلى العشاء . حين غاب الشفق . ثم صلى العشاء الآخرة حين ذهب ثـلـث الـلـيـل ثـم صلى الصبح حين اسفرت الارض ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء مواقيت الصلوة عن النبي ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ رابوداؤد شریف، باب المواقیت،ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء کی نماز شفق غائب ہونے کے بعد پڑھی۔ (۳) اور آخر وقت صبح صادق سے پہلے تک ہے اسکی دلیل اس حدیث کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت اعتم النبى الله ذات ليلة حتى ذهــب عـامـة الليل وحتى نام اهل المسجد (مسلم شریف، باب وقت العشاء وتاً خیرھا،ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۶۳۸ ۱۴۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عامۃ المیل رات کا ایک بڑا حصہ چلا گیا۔ (۴) اور آخر رات تک عشا کے وقت ہونے کی دلیل صحابہ کا قول ہے۔ رويناعن ابن عباس انه قال : وقت العشاء الى الفجر ـ و عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف في امرأة تطهر قبل طلوع الفجر صلت المغرب والعشاء قال لابى هريرة ما افراط صلوة العشاء؟ قال طلوع الفجر
(السنن البيهقي ، باب آخر وقت الجواز لصلوۃ العشاء، ج اول ص ۵۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۶۳) صحابی کے اس قول سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کا وقت طلوع فجر سے پہلے تک ہے۔ تمام ائمہ کا یہی مسلک ہے۔
Prayer times: Time of Isha the last. From this effect it is known that after the whiteness of the horizon disappears, i.e., after the white twilight sets, the time for Isha prayer occurs. (4) From the allusion of this verse one can deduce: 'Establish prayer from the declining of the sun to the darkness of the night and the recital of the dawn' (Surah Al-Isra 17:78). In this verse is 'darkness of the night', meaning when darkness comes then pray Isha, which indicates that after the white twilight sets is the time for Isha because complete blackness occurs only at that time. And before that is the time for Maghrib. The proof of the two companions (Sahibayn): According to the Sahibayn and the majority of imams, the redness before the spreading whiteness is the time for Maghrib. (1) Their proof is this hadith: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The twilight is the redness; when the twilight disappears, prayer becomes obligatory.' (Darqutni, Bab fi sifat al-Maghrib wa asbah, vol. 1, p. 276, no. 1044; and also al-Bayhaqi, Bab dukhul waqt al-isha bi ghaybubat al-shafaq, vol. 1, p. 548, no. 1744) This hadith shows that Maghrib time extends until the red twilight. (2) There is an effect: From Ibn Umar, he said: 'The twilight is the redness.' (Darqutni, Bab fi sifat al-Maghrib wa asbah, vol. 1, p. 276, no. 1045; also al-Bayhaqi, Bab dukhul waqt al-isha bi ghaybubat al-shafaq, vol. 1, p. 548, no. 1742) In this effect also, twilight is the redness. What is the red twilight and white twilight? Red twilight and white twilight: After sunset, first redness appears, then there is a spread-out white light called 'bayad mustatir' because it is spread out. After that, this white light becomes elongated called 'bayad mustatil' because it is elongated light. After that, complete darkness covers the horizon. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the redness, the spread-out whiteness (bayad mustatir) is the time for Maghrib. After that, the time for Isha begins. How does twilight occur? Near the horizon there is much vapor and moisture. When the sun sets, its light passes through the vapor and moisture and comes towards us. The rule is that when light passes through vapor, it appears red and slightly spread. Therefore, after sunset, the light seen is red, called red twilight. But when the sun goes twelve degrees below, the light does not pass through the vapor and moisture near the horizon; rather, the sun's light appears elongated towards the sky. Since it does not pass through vapor and moisture, that light appears white and very faint. After the red twilight, continue watching, then it will be known; otherwise, it is not known quickly. This is called white twilight. This humble one has experienced it many times in his country Jharkhand. (The commentator is an expert astronomer) Translation (300): [5] The time for Isha and Witr is from there until true dawn. Explanation: According to the saying of the Sahibayn, after the red twilight, and according to the saying of Imam A'zam, after the white twilight, the time for Isha begins and remains until true dawn. Reasoning: (1) Several hadiths have passed regarding the beginning of Isha time. (2) In this hadith also: From Ibn Abbas, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Jibril led me twice at the Kaaba... then he prayed Isha when the twilight disappeared, then he prayed the last Isha when one-third of the night had passed, then he prayed Fajr when the earth became bright, then he turned to Jibril and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi mawaqit al-salat 'an al-nabi, p. 42, no. 149; Abu Dawud, Bab al-mawaqit, p. 68, no. 393) In this hadith, Isha prayer was offered after the twilight disappeared. (3) And the end time is before true dawn, its proof is the indication of this hadith: From Aisha, she said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed one night until most of the night had passed and until the people of the mosque slept.' (Muslim, Bab waqt al-isha wa ta'khiriha, p. 257, no. 638/1445) This hadith shows that 'ammat al-layl' (most of the night) means a large portion of the night passed. (4) And the proof that Isha time extends to the end of the night is the saying of the companions. We narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'The time for Isha is until dawn.' And from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf regarding a woman who became pure before dawn and prayed Maghrib and Isha, he said to Abu Huraira: 'What is the extreme time of Isha prayer?' He said: 'Dawn.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab akhar waqt al-jawaz li salat al-isha, vol. 1, p. 553, no. 1763) From this saying of a companion, it is known that Isha time is until before dawn. All imams have this same madhhab.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of shafaq (twilight) and its impact on the start of Isha prayer time. The author first presents the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, who takes shafaq abyad (white twilight) as the end of Maghrib and beginning of Isha. He supports this with the Quranic verse 'to the darkness of the night' indicating complete darkness after white twilight. Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the majority of scholars are presented, who define shafaq as red twilight (shafaq ahmar) and thus Maghrib time ends when the redness disappears. Their proof includes the hadith 'the twilight is the redness' and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported in the Jibril hadith where he prayed Isha when the twilight disappeared. The author then explains the physical phenomena of red and white twilight, noting that according to Abu Hanifa, the spread-out whiteness (bayad mustatir) is still Maghrib time, while the Sahibayn consider the redness as the boundary. After presenting both positions, the author affirms that the time for Isha and Witr extends from the disappearance of shafaq (according to each view) until true dawn (subh sadiq). This is supported by multiple hadith and companion statements showing that Isha may be delayed until the last third of the night and is valid until dawn. The passage thus clarifies that while the start time differs, the end time is agreed upon. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, defining shafaq as redness, which is the majority view.

Key Terms
شفق (shafaq): Twilight; the light remaining after sunset at the horizon. In this passage, it is either red (ahmar) or white (abyad) depending on the view.
شفق احمر (shafaq ahmar): Red twilight that appears right after sunset; it is the spread-out redness on the horizon.
شفق ابیض (shafaq abyad): White twilight that appears after the red twilight; it is fainter and more vertical (bayad mustatil).
بیاض مستطیر (bayad mustatir): Spread-out whiteness; a horizontal white light after sunset, before the elongated white light.
بیاض مستطیل (bayad mustatil): Elongated whiteness; a vertical white light rising from the horizon, signaling the start of Isha according to Abu Hanifa.
غسق اللیل (ghasaq al-layl): Darkness of the night; used as a Quranic term to indicate the time of Isha prayer.
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, when does the time for Isha prayer begin?
A) When the white twilight (shafaq abyad) disappears
B) When the red twilight (shafaq ahmar) disappears
C) When the sun is twelve degrees below the horizon
D) When complete darkness covers the horizon

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling defines shafaq as red twilight, so Isha time begins when the red twilight disappears and ends at true dawn.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Witr Not Preceded Before Isha Due to Necessary Order
Ruling that witr must be prayed after Isha, not before, due to established order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that witr must be prayed after Isha, explain the exception for accidental reversal, and apply the principle that witr is not subordinate to Isha.

Core Idea
Witr must be prayed after Isha, but if accidentally reversed, witr remains valid.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling about the sequence between the Isha and witr prayers. While the order is necessary (tartib lazim), the Hanafi school makes an important distinction: witr is not dependent on Isha for its validity. This nuance has practical implications when mistakes occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the order of witr and Isha
State the basic ruling: witr should not be prayed before Isha due to the necessary order (tartib lazim). The matn explicitly says 'لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء'.
This ruling is based on the hadith of Jibril.
2
Understand the evidence (dalil)
The order is established from hadith, which shows that witr is prayed after Isha. The commentary refers to this hadith as the proof.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Grasp the exception: witr is not subordinate
Despite the necessary order, witr is not tabi' (subordinate) to Isha. This means its validity does not depend on Isha being valid. If witr is accidentally prayed before Isha, it remains valid.
Key term: تابع (tabi')
4
Apply the example
Work through the given scenario: one prays Isha without wudu, then later prays witr with wudu, then discovers Isha was invalid. They repeat Isha but do not need to repeat witr.
This illustrates that witr is independent of Isha.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider witr as sunnah, not wajib, so the order is recommended but not as binding. However, they agree on the sequence.
The practical difference is in the level of sin for deliberate reversal.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۳۰۱) ترتیب لازم ہونے کی وجہ سے وتر کو عشاء پر مقدم نہ کیا جائے۔
تشریح : حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ وتر عشاء کے بعد ہے، چونکہ وتر اور عشاء میں ترتیب لازم ہے اس لئے وتر کو عشاء سے پہلے نہ پڑھے بلکہ بعد میں ہی پڑھے ،لیکن وتر عشاء کے تابع نہیں ہے اس لئے کسی غلطی کی وجہ سے وتر کو پہلے پڑھ لیا تو وتر کو دوبارہ لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے وتر ہو گیا، مثلا عشاء کی نماز پڑھی ، پھر وضو کر کے وتر کی نماز پڑھی ، بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ عشاء کی نماز بغیر وضو کے پڑھی تھی اس لئے عشاء کی نماز لوٹائی تو اب و تر کولوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ ہو گیا۔
Translation (301): Due to the necessary order, witr should not be preceded over Isha. Explanation: From hadith it is clear that witr is after Isha. Since the order between witr and Isha is necessary, one should not pray witr before Isha but rather after it. However, witr is not subordinate to Isha, so if due to a mistake witr was prayed first, there is no need to repeat witr; witr is valid. For example: One prayed Isha prayer, then performed wudu and prayed witr. Later it was discovered that Isha prayer was prayed without wudu, so Isha prayer is repeated but there is no need to repeat witr because it has been done.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanation on the order between Isha and witr prayers. The matn states that witr should not be prayed before Isha due to the necessary order (tartib lazim). The commentary explains that this order is established from hadith, which shows that witr is prayed after Isha. Therefore, the sequence must be observed: Isha first, then witr. However, the commentator clarifies an important nuance: witr is not subordinate to Isha in terms of validity. This means that if someone erroneously prays witr before Isha, witr is still valid and does not need to be repeated. The example given illustrates this: if a person prays Isha without wudu (invalid), then later performs wudu and prays witr, and then discovers that the original Isha was invalid, they must repeat Isha but do not need to repeat witr. This is because witr, though ordered after Isha, is an independent prayer. Thus, while the order is necessary (i.e., it is sinful to deliberately reverse it), accidental reversal does not invalidate witr.

Key Terms
ترتیب لازم (tartib lazim): Necessary order; a required sequence in prayer times where one prayer must be performed before another, and reversing the order is not permissible without reason.
مقدم نہ کیا جائے (muqaddam na kiya jaye): Should not be preceded; meaning witr should not be offered before Isha.
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate; dependent on another for validity. Witr is not tabi' of Isha, meaning its validity does not depend on Isha being valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone accidentally prays witr before Isha, what is the ruling on witr?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid and does not need to be repeated.
C) It is invalid but does not need to be repeated.
D) It becomes a nafl prayer.

Key Takeaway
Witr must be prayed after Isha, but if accidentally reversed, witr remains valid because it is not subordinate to Isha.

Time of Isha and Witr Prayer
States the time of Isha and Witr from after twilight until dawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Isha and Witr according to the Hanafi school, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the evidence for the end time.

Core Idea
Isha time begins after twilight and lasts until dawn; the start differs within the school.

In this passage, the author lays out the ruling for the time of Isha and Witr, citing evidence from hadith and Companion statements. Understanding this time boundary is essential for correctly performing the obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The time window for Isha and Witr prayers.
The ruling determines validity: praying before the time invalidates the prayer.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the beginning
Identify the two views: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) vs Imam Abu Hanifa on which twilight marks the start.
Sahibayn: after red twilight (shafaq ahmar); Abu Hanifa: after white twilight (shafaq abyad).
3
Analyze the evidence for the beginning
Examine the hadith of Ibn Abbas (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) where Jibril led the Prophet and prayed Isha 'when the twilight disappeared'.
The phrase 'when the twilight disappeared' is interpreted differently based on which twilight.
4
Analyze the evidence for the end time
Examine the hadith of Aisha (Muslim) and Companions' statements (Bayhaqi) showing that Isha time extends to dawn.
The hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet delaying Isha until most of the night passed, indicating time extends beyond midnight.
5
Note the agreed end time
All Hanafi imams agree that the end of Isha time is at true dawn (fajr sadiq).
This is supported by the statement of Ibn Abbas and others.

ثمرة النجاح جلد ا ۲۱۲ اوقات الصلوة (۳۰۰) والعشاء والوتر منه الى الصبح. مسلسل دیکھتے رہیں تب اس کا پتہ چلے گا ورنہ جلدی پتہ نہیں چلتا۔ اس کو شفق ابیض کہتے ہیں۔ ناچیز نے اس کا تجربہ کئی بار اپنے ملک جھار کھنڈ میں کیا ہے۔ ( شارح ماہر فلکیات ہیں ) ترجمه : ( ۳۰۰) عشاء اور وتر کا وقت وہاں سے صبح صادق تک ہے۔ تشریح : صاحبین کے قول پر شفق احمد کے بعد ، اور امام اعظم کے قول پر شفق ابیض کے بعد عشاء کا وقت شروع ہوتا ہے اور صبح صادق تک رہتا ہے وجه : (۱) عشاء کے اول وقت کے سلسلے میں کئی حدیثیں گزرگئیں ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عباس ان النبی صلی الله علیه وسلم قال امنی جبرئیل عند البيت مرتين .... ثم صلى العشاء . حين غاب الشفق . ثم صلى العشاء الآخرة حين ذهب ثـلـث الـلـيـل ثـم صلى الصبح حين اسفرت الارض ثم التفت الى جبرئيل فقال يا محمد هذا وقت الانبياء من قبلك والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء مواقيت الصلوة عن النبي ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۱۴۹ رابوداؤد شریف، باب المواقیت،ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عشاء کی نماز شفق غائب ہونے کے بعد پڑھی۔ (۳) اور آخر وقت صبح صادق سے پہلے تک ہے اسکی دلیل اس حدیث کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت اعتم النبى صلی الله علیه وسلم ذات ليلة حتى ذهــب عـامـة الليل وحتى نام اهل المسجد (مسلم شریف، باب وقت العشاء وتاً خیرھا،ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۶۳۸ ۱۴۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عامۃ المیل رات کا ایک بڑا حصہ چلا گیا۔ (۴) اور آخر رات تک عشا کے وقت ہونے کی دلیل صحابہ کا قول ہے۔ روینا عن ابن عباس انه قال : وقت العشاء الى الفجر ـ و عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف في امرأة تطهر قبل طلوع الفجر صلت المغرب والعشاء قال لابى هريرة ما افراط صلوة العشاء؟ قال طلوع الفجر (السنن سبیھقی ، باب آخر وقت الجواز لصلوۃ العشاء، ج اول ص ۵۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۶۳) صحابی کے اس قول سے معلوم ہوا کہ عشا کا وقت طلوع فجر سے پہلے تک ہے۔ تمام ائمہ کا یہی مسلک ہے۔
(300) And the Isha and Witr are until dawn. Translation: The time for Isha and Witr is from that time until true dawn. Explanation: According to the Sahibayn, Isha time begins after the red twilight, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the white twilight, and it lasts until true dawn. Evidence: (1) Several hadith have passed regarding the beginning of Isha time. (2) In this hadith: Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet said: 'Jibril led me twice at the house... then he prayed Isha when the twilight disappeared, then he prayed the later Isha when one-third of the night had passed, then he prayed Fajr when the earth became bright...' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). This indicates Isha prayer after the twilight is gone. (3) The end time is before true dawn, as indicated in the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet delayed Isha one night until most of the night had passed...' (Muslim). (4) The end of Isha time until dawn is supported by the sayings of the Companions: Ibn Abbas said: 'The time of Isha is until dawn'; Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf said regarding a woman who became pure before dawn and prayed Maghrib and Isha; Abu Hurairah said: 'The end of Isha time is dawn.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This shows the time of Isha is until before the appearance of dawn. All imams agree.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time for Isha and Witr prayers. The author begins by stating the ruling: the time for Isha and Witr extends from the disappearance of twilight until true dawn. He then explains the difference between the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on the beginning of Isha: according to the Sahibayn, it begins after the red twilight (shafaq ahmar); according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the white twilight (shafaq abyad). Both agree the time ends at dawn. The author provides four proofs: (1) He references earlier hadith that passed. (2) The well-known hadith of Ibn Abbas about Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer, showing that Isha was prayed after the twilight disappeared. (3) The hadith of Aisha showing the Prophet delayed Isha until a large portion of the night had passed, indicating the time extends. (4) Statements of the Companions Ibn Abbas, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, and Abu Hurairah equating the end of Isha time with the appearance of dawn. The author notes that all imams follow this view.

Key Terms
الشفق (ash-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; either the red or white glow before complete darkness.
الشفق الاحمر (ash-shafaq al-ahmar): The red twilight that appears immediately after sunset.
الشفق الابیض (ash-shafaq al-abyad): The white twilight that appears after the red twilight fades.
صبح صادق (subh sadiq): True dawn, the second dawn that spreads horizontally across the horizon, marking the end of Isha and start of Fajr.
عشاء (isha): The night prayer, the fifth of the obligatory prayers.
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does the time for Isha prayer begin?
A) After the red twilight disappears
B) After the white twilight disappears
C) At sunset
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
Isha time begins after twilight and ends at dawn; the Hanafi school has two views on which twilight marks the start, but the end is unanimously dawn.

Ruling on Isha and Witr When Time is Absent
Ruling on Isha and Witr when time not found

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Isha and Witr when their time is absent and apply the principle of estimation based on the hadith of Nawwas ibn Sam'an.

Core Idea
When the time for a prayer is completely absent, the obligation is lifted; estimation is the Hanafi solution.

This lesson deals with a unique scenario: Muslims living in polar regions where the sun does not set or sets only briefly. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that time is the cause (sabab) for prayer obligation. When the cause is absent, the effect (obligation) is also absent. However, the hadith of the Dajjal instructs estimation during abnormal days, leading to a practical solution that balances obligation and ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act (Isha and Witr) and the ruling when time is absent: they are not obligatory. Then note the recommendation to estimate in abnormal conditions.
The ruling depends on the presence of time as a cause.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith of Nawwas ibn Sam'an cited in the text. It provides the basis for estimation.
The hadith is about the Dajjal's days, analogized to polar days.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command 'aqdiru lahu qadrahu' (estimate its measure) shows that when actual time is unavailable, one must approximate it.
This indicates that estimation is a legitimate method in fiqh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars hold that if time is absent, the prayer is simply not obligatory. The Hanafi school responds by citing the hadith and adopting estimation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Apply the two scenarios
Distinguish between (1) sun not setting at all (Maghrib, Isha, Fajr estimated) and (2) sun sets briefly but no shariah night (Maghrib and Fajr obligatory, Isha estimated).
The estimation method uses times from the nearest moderate region.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۰۲) اور جو لوگ عشا و وتر کے وقت کو نہ پائے ان پر یہ دونوں واجب نہیں۔ تشریح : اس مسئلے کی بنیاد یہ ہے کہ وقت نمازوں کے لئے سبب ہے، اور جب وقت نہیں پایا گیا تو عشاء اور وتر بھی واجب نہیں ہوں گی۔ لیکن کچھ حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ معتدل دنوں میں جس طرح نماز پڑھتے ہیں اس کا اندازہ کر کے نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اندازہ کر کے نماز پڑھی جائے . عن النواس بن سمعان الكلابي قال ذکر رسول الله الدجال ..... و ما لبثه في الارض قال اربعون يوما ، يوم كسنة و يوم كشهر ، و يوم كجمعة ، و سائر أيـامـه كـايامكم ، قلنا يا رسول الله ! هذا اليوم الذى كسنة أتكفينا فيه صلاة يوم و ليلة ؟ قال : لا ، اقدروا له قدره (ابوداود شریف ، باب خروج الدجال ،ص ۶۰۷ نمبر ۴۳۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی فدیہ الرجال، ص ۵۱۳، نمبر ۲۲۴۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جو دن ایک سال کے برابر ہو اس میں اندازہ کر کے پورے سال کی نمازیں ادا کریں۔ نوٹ : عشاء کا وقت نہ ہونے کی دو صورتیں ہیں [1] ایک تو یہ کہ سورج ڈوبے ہی نہیں، جیسے ساڑھے چھیاسٹھ ڈگری سے نوے ڈگری کے درمیان ہوتا ہے کہ کچھ دنوں میں سورج ڈوبتا ہی نہیں تو یہاں مغرب، عشاء، اور فجر اندازہ کر کے پڑھی جائے ، اور رمضان کا روزہ سردی میں قضاء کر کے رکھا جائے ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ آفتاب تھوڑی دیر کے لئے ڈوبے، لیکن شفق ابیض ڈوبنے کے بعد اور صبح صادق ہونے سے پہلے جو اندھیری رات ہوتی ہے جسکولیل شرعی کا نام دیا جاتا ہے] جو عشاء کا وقت ہوتا ہے وہ نہ ہوتو اس میں مغرب اور فجر کا وقت آیا اس لئے یہ دونوں واجب ہوں گے ، اور عشاء کی نماز اندازہ کر کے جس میں امت کو سہولت ہو اس میں پڑھے۔
(302) And those who do not find the time for Isha and Witr, these two are not obligatory upon them. Explanation: The basis of this issue is that time is the cause for prayers, and when the time is not found, Isha and Witr are not obligatory. However, some scholars hold that one should estimate the time as in moderate days and pray accordingly. Evidence: The hadith of Nawwas ibn Sam'an al-Kilabi: The Prophet mentioned the Dajjal and his stay on earth of forty days: a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, and the rest like your days. They asked: 'O Messenger of Allah, on the day like a year, will the prayers of one day and night suffice us?' He said: 'No, estimate its measure.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Note: There are two scenarios when Isha time is not found: [1] The sun does not set (e.g., in regions between 66.5° and 90° latitude). In this case, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr are prayed by estimation, and Ramadan fasts are made up in winter. [2] The sun sets briefly but there is no period of complete darkness (shafaq abyad disappears but dawn does not appear properly). Here Maghrib and Fajr times exist, so they are obligatory. For Isha, one estimates and prays it at a time when the community finds ease.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage addresses a special case: when a person lives in a region where the sun does not set or sets so briefly that the time for Isha (and Witr) does not occur. The author establishes the principle that time is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayers. If the time is absent, there is no obligation. However, the author then presents the view of some scholars (another school or some Hanafis) who advocate estimation based on the hadith of the Dajjal, where the Prophet instructed to estimate prayer times during unusual days. The author provides two practical scenarios: (1) The sun does not set at all, typical in polar regions during summer. In this case, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr are prayed by estimation (estimating the duration from sunset to dawn from moderate regions). Ramadan fasts cannot be kept at their actual time; they are made up in winter. (2) The sun sets briefly but there is no 'shariah night' (the period of total darkness after white twilight disappears and before dawn). Here Maghrib and Fajr are still observable because their times depend on sunset and dawn. Isha, which depends on darkness, is not found, so it is prayed by estimation at a time suitable for the community. The author's note clarifies the latitude range (66.5° to 90°) where these phenomena occur.

Key Terms
الليل الشرعي (al-layl ash-shar'i): The period of complete darkness after the white twilight disappears until the appearance of true dawn, which is the time for Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a region where the sun does not set for several days, how should a Hanafi perform Isha and Fajr?
A) They are not obligatory at all.
B) They are prayed at the same time as Maghrib.
C) They are estimated based on the nearest region with normal times.
D) They are prayed when the sun sets, even if not visible.

Key Takeaway
When time for Isha and Witr is absent, the Hanafi school rules that they are not obligatory but recommends estimation based on normal times.
